Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
6 min
Agent for Ijarah: Authority to Collect Rent
Clarifies whether an agent for lease has the right to collect rent and hold the lessee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the authority of an agent for ijarah to collect rent and determine the validity of waiving rent or canceling the lease.

Core Idea
An agent for ijarah has full authority to collect rent and detain the lessee; this is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.

When you appoint an agent to lease your property, does that agent have the right to collect the rent on your behalf? Or must you handle all payments personally? This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq settles an intra-Hanafi dispute, affirming that the agent for lease (وكيل بالإجارة) indeed has the authority to collect rent, detain the lessee for non-payment, and even cancel the lease before the tenant takes possession. Understanding this authority is essential for both principals and agents in lease transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the act
Determine what exactly is being ruled upon: the authority of an agent for ijarah to collect rent, detain the lessee, waive rent, and cancel the lease.
The act is the agent's exercise of agency powers.
2
Locate the evidence and its weight
The correct view is from Kafi al-Hakim, which is based on the text of Imam Muhammad, part of Zahir al-Riwayah. The opposing view from Munyat al-Mufti is dismissed as a slip.
Zahir al-Riwayah is the most authoritative layer in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyze the specific powers: collection, detention, waiver
The agent can litigate for rent, collect it, and detain the lessee. Waiver of rent before collection is valid only if the rent is a debt (not a specific item). If it is a specific item, waiver is invalid and the agent guarantees it.
Cancellation of the lease before use discharges the lessee unless rent was already collected.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and tarjih
Munyat al-Mufti denied the agent's authority, but the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq overrules it as a mistake. The mufta bihi is the Kafi al-Hakim view.
This illustrates how later scholars resolve conflicts between earlier texts.
5
Apply the ruling to analogous situations
The passage analogizes the agent for ijarah to the agent for purchase (وكيل بالشراء) regarding liability and demands. This helps extend the ruling to similar agency contexts.
The agent's authority is comparable to that of a purchasing agent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وظاهر كلام المصنف أن للوكيل بالإجارة قبض الأجرة وعليه تسليم العين إلى المستأجر، وفي منية المفتي خلافه قال الوكيل بالإجارة ليس له قبض الأجرة وحبس المستأجر به ولو وهب الأجرة قبل القبض جاز إن لم يكن شيئاً بعينه ا هـ. وهو سبق قلم والصواب ما في كافي الحاكم أن للوكيل بالإجارة المخاصمة في إثباتها وقبض الأجرة وحبس المستأجر به فإن وهب الأجرة قبل القبض جاز إن لم يكن بعينه ويضمنه وإن كان بعينه لا. وإن ناقض الوكيل المستأجر الإجارة قبل أن يعمل فيها شيئاً جازت ديناً كان الأجر أو عيناً وبرئ المستأجر إلا أن يكون الوكيل قبض الأجر ا.هـ. وعلى هذا يطالب الوكيل بالاستئجار بالأجرة كالوكيل بالشراء
And the apparent meaning of the author's statement is that the agent for ijarah has the right to collect the rent and is responsible for handing over the property to the lessee. In Munyat al-Mufti, there is a contrary view: 'The agent for ijarah does not have the right to collect the rent and detain the lessee with it; and if he waives the rent before collection, it is valid if it is not a specific thing.' That is a slip of the pen. The correct view is what is in Kafi al-Hakim: that the agent for ijarah has the right to litigation for its establishment, collection of the rent, and detaining the lessee with it. If he waives the rent before collection, it is valid if it is not a specific thing, and he guarantees it if it is specific. And if the agent cancels the ijarah with the lessee before he has done anything in it, it is valid whether the rent was a debt or a specific thing, and the lessee is discharged unless the agent had collected the rent. And accordingly, the agent is demanded to hire with the rent like the agent for purchase.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe that clarifies the authority of an agent for lease (وكيل بالإجارة). The base text (Kanz al-Daqaiq) implies that the agent has the right to collect rent and must deliver the property. The author notes a contrary view in Munyat al-Mufti, which denies the agent's right to collect rent and detain the lessee. However, the author dismisses this as a slip of the pen (سبق قلم) and states the correct view is from Kafi al-Hakim, based on the text of Imam Muhammad. The correct view grants the agent authority to litigate for the rent, collect it, and detain the lessee for payment. If the agent waives the rent before collection, it is valid only if the rent is not a specific item (i.e., if it is a debt); if it is a specific item, the waiver is invalid and the agent is liable. Additionally, if the agent cancels the ijarah before the lessee has used the property, the cancellation is valid regardless of whether the rent was a debt or a specific item, and the lessee is discharged from the rent unless the agent had already collected it. This shows that the agent's role is analogous to the agent for purchase regarding liability and demand.

Key Terms
وكيل بالإجارة (wakeel bil ijarah): An agent appointed to lease out a property or to lease a property for the principal.
قبض الأجرة (qabd al-ujra): Taking possession of the rent payment, including actual receipt.
ناقض الإجارة (naqada al-ijarah): To cancel or rescind the lease contract by mutual agreement or unilateral action where permitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in Kafi al-Hakim, can an agent for ijarah waive the rent before collection if the rent is a specific item?
A) Yes, it is valid and the agent is discharged.
B) No, it is invalid and the agent guarantees it.
C) Yes, but only if the principal agrees.
D) No, but the agent is not liable.

Key Takeaway
An agent for ijarah has inherent authority to collect rent, waive non-specific rent, and cancel before use, as established in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Cancelling Hire Before Work by the Agent-Hirer
Ruling on cancellation of hire by agent-hirer before work begins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an agent-hirer cancels the hire before work begins and identify the exception when the agent has already received the wage.

Core Idea
Cancelling a hire before work is valid, but if the agent already took the wage, he remains liable.

This ruling from Al-Khulasa addresses a specific agency scenario: an agent (wakīl musta'jar) is hired by a principal to employ a worker. The agent later cancels the hire contract before any work is performed. The text clarifies that such cancellation is valid, regardless of whether the wage was a debt or a specific item. However, an important exception arises if the agent had already collected the wage from the principal—in that case, the agent remains obligated to either hire someone or return the wage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the contract
Recognize the three parties: the principal (who wants a worker), the agent-hirer (who is delegated to hire), and the worker (who would be hired). The contract in question is the hire (ijara) between the agent and the worker.
The agent acts on behalf of the principal; the worker is to be hired by the agent.
2
State the general rule
The cancellation of the hire by the agent before any work is performed is valid (ja'iz). This applies whether the wage was specified as a debt (dhan) or a specific tangible item (ayn). The principal is discharged from any obligation.
The wage type does not affect the permissibility of cancellation.
3
Identify the exception
If the agent had already received the wage from the principal, the cancellation does not free the agent from liability. The agent must either proceed with hiring or return the wage.
The agent's receipt of the wage creates a duty to use it for the intended purpose or return it.
4
Understand the analogy
The author compares the agent-hirer to an agent for purchase (wakīl bil-shira'). Just as a purchase agent must use the principal's funds to buy, the agent-hirer must use the wage to hire. This reinforces the agent's obligation to execute the delegated task with the principal's assets.
This analogy is a qiyas based on the common 'illa of agency requiring faithful execution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن ناقض الوكيل المستأجر الإجارة قبل أن يعمل فيها شيئاً جازت ديناً كان الأجر أو عيناً وبرئ المستأجر إلا أن يكون الوكيل قبض الأجر ا.هـ. وعلى هذا يطالب الوكيل بالاستئجار بالأجرة كالوكيل بالشراء.
And if the agent who is hired [by the principal to hire someone] cancels the hire before he has done any work in it, it is permissible, whether the wage was a debt or a specific item, and the hirer [the original principal] is discharged, unless the agent [the middleman] had received the wage. End of quote. And on this basis, the agent is required to hire [someone] with the wage, like the agent for purchase.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Al-Khulasa concerning an agent who is authorized to hire someone (e.g., a worker) but then cancels the hire contract before any work is performed. The ruling states that such cancellation is valid regardless of whether the wage was specified as a debt (dhan) or a specific tangible item (ayn). The principal (the original hirer) is freed from any obligation. However, if the agent had already collected the wage from the principal, then cancellation does not discharge the agent; he remains liable to return it or proceed. The author then analogizes: just as an agent for purchase is required to pay the price from the principal's funds, the agent-hirer is similarly required to use the wage to hire someone.

Key Terms
الوكيل المستأجر (al-wakīl al-musta'jar): An agent who is appointed by the principal to hire a third party (e.g., a worker) on behalf of the principal.
الإجارة (al-ījārah): Hire contract; a lease or employment agreement for services or usufruct.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an agent hired to employ a worker cancels the hire contract before any work is done, but the agent had already received the wage from the principal, what is the ruling?
A) The cancellation is invalid and the agent must proceed with hiring.
B) The cancellation is valid but the agent must return the wage.
C) The cancellation is valid and the agent is free of liability.
D) The cancellation is only valid if the wage was a debt.

Key Takeaway
An agent-hirer can cancel the hire before work begins, but if he already received the wage, he remains liable.

Self-Help for Specific Property in Hanafi Fiqh
Rulings on self-help when the right is a tangible object

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two cases where self-help is permitted for specific tangible property and apply the conditions for liability when cutting encroaching branches.

Core Idea
Self-help is permitted for specific property when court order is impractical or harm prevention is proportional.

This lesson explores two examples from the Hanafi school where a person may take direct action to assert property rights without a judge's order. In the first case, a landlord whose tenant has disappeared may re-enter and re-let the property. In the second, a homeowner may cut encroaching tree branches if the owner cannot remedy the situation. These rulings illustrate how necessity and harm prevention override the general requirement for judicial intervention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and identify the two distinct cases: (1) missing tenant with belongings, (2) tree branches encroaching airspace.
The first is from al-Quniyya, the second from Muniya al-Mufti.
2
Extract conditions for missing tenant case
Note that the tenant disappeared after the rental period ended, leaving belongings. The landlord may make a new key, re-enter, and even re-rent without court permission. The belongings are set aside. Identify the operative principle: the right is to a specific object (the house), and necessity overrides the need for court order.
3
Extract conditions for tree branch case
If branches encroach, the homeowner may cut them. Liability depends on whether the branch owner could have tied them back. If possible, the cutter is liable. If not possible, and a judge would have ordered cutting, then no liability. Identify the condition: proportionality and reasonable alternative.
4
Synthesize the principle
Both cases show that self-help is justified when the right is clear and certain, and either court order is impracticable or the judge would have ordered the same action. The common thread is preventing harm or loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان عيناً ففي إجارة القنية : ولو غاب المستأجر بعد السنة ولم يسلم المفتاح إلى الآخر فله أن يتخذ له مفتاحاً آخر، ولو أجره من غيره بغير إذن الحاكم جاز ا هـ . وقد صارت حادثة الفتوى مضت المدة وغاب المستأجر وترك متاعه في الدار فأفتيت بأن له أن يفتح الدار ويسكن فيها، وأما المتاع فيجعله في ناحية إلى حضور صاحبه ولا يتوقف الفتح على إذن القاضي أخذاً مما في القنية وفي غصب منية المفتي : أخذت أغصان شجرة إنسان هواء دار آخر فقطع رب الدار الأغصان، فإن كانت الأغصان بحالة يمكن لصاحبها إن يشدها بحبل ويفرغ هواء داره ضمن القاطع، وإن لم يمكن لا يضمن إذا قطع من موضع لو رفع إلى الحاكم أمر بالقطع من ذلك الموضع ا هـ.
If it is a specific thing, then in Ijarah of al-Quniyya: If the tenant disappears after the year and does not hand over the key to the other, the landlord may make another key for himself. And if he rents it to someone else without the permission of the judge, it is permissible, etc. And a case for fatwa occurred: the period passed and the tenant disappeared, leaving his belongings in the house, and I gave the fatwa that the landlord may open the house and live in it, and as for the belongings, he should put them aside until the owner appears; and opening does not depend on the judge's permission, taking this from al-Quniyya. And in Ghasp of Muniya al-Mufti: If the branches of a person's tree take up the airspace of another's house, and the owner of the house cuts the branches, then if the branches are in a state that their owner could tie them with a rope and free the airspace of the house, then the cutter is liable. But if not possible, he is not liable if he cuts from a place such that if it were referred to the judge, he would order cutting from that place, etc.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage presents two scenarios where a person may take action with respect to a specific object without court order. First, in the case of a missing tenant, the landlord may make a new key, enter the house, rent it to another, and even dispose of the tenant's belongings by setting them aside. This is based on necessity and the impracticality of obtaining a judge's order. Second, regarding encroaching tree branches: if the branches can be removed by the owner (by tying them back), then the neighbor who cuts them is liable (for damages). If they cannot be removed reasonably, and a judge would order cutting anyway, then the neighbor may cut them without liability. This aligns with the principle that one may prevent harm if the judge would likely order it.

Key Terms
عين ('ayn): A specific, tangible object as opposed to a debt or right.
إجارة (ijara): Lease or rental contract.
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation; taking another's property wrongfully.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a neighbor cuts tree branches that encroach on his airspace, and the branches could have been tied back by the owner?
A) The neighbor is liable for damages.
B) The neighbor is not liable.
C) The neighbor must first get a judge's order.
D) The owner of the tree must pay the neighbor.

Key Takeaway
Self-help for a specific tangible object is permitted when the right is clear and either a court order is impracticable or the judge would have ordered the same action.

Mutual Oaths in Ijarah Disputes Before Utilization
Ruling on mutual oaths in hire dispute before utilization, with details of oath beginning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mutual oaths in ijarah disputes before utilization and determine which party begins the oath based on the subject of the dispute.

Core Idea
In ijarah disputes before the benefit is used, mutual oaths apply; the denier swears first.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling for disagreements that arise in a hire contract before the hirer has received the service. The text establishes that mutual oaths (tahalf) are required, analogous to sale before possession, and provides detailed guidance on who swears first depending on whether the dispute is over the rent or the benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope of the ruling
Note that the ruling applies specifically to disputes in ijarah contracts before the benefit has been utilized (istifa').
After utilization, different rules may apply.
2
Recognize the analogical basis
The ruling is based on qiyas: just as mutual oaths are taken in sale before possession, they are taken in ijarah before utilization.
The illa is the incomplete execution of the contract.
3
Distinguish between disputes over rent and benefit
If the dispute is about the rent amount, the hirer (musta'jir) is the denier of the obligation and begins the oath. If about the benefit (e.g., quality), the lessor (mu'ajjir) is the denier and begins.
The denier is the one who would lose if no evidence is given.
4
Apply the starting party rule
Once the subject is identified, the denier swears first. If they refuse (nukul), the other party's claim is upheld.
Evidence can override oaths; if both give evidence, the lessor's evidence on rent is preferred, the hirer's on benefit.
5
Note the exceptions
There are exceptions: e.g., when the owner claims rent and the occupant denies, the word is with the occupant. Also, in caravanserai cases, the default fatwa is that rent is due unless known otherwise.
These exceptions are found in Munyat al-Mufti and al-Bazzaziyya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو اختلفا في الإجارة قبل الاستيفاء تحالفا) لأن التحالف في البيع قبل القبض على وفق القياس والإجارة قبل الاستيفاء نظيره أطلقه فشمل الاختلاف في البدل أو المبدل كما في الهداية، ومع القصار كما في منية المفتي ولا يشمل ما إذا ادعى المالك الأجر ونفاه الساكن والقول للمستأجر، وكذا إذا نزل الخان واختلفا والفتوى على وجوب الأجر إلا إذا عرف بخلافه وتمامه في البزازية. وفي التهذيب : الاختلاف في قدر يوجب التحالف اهـ. فإن وقع الاختلاف في الأجرة بدأ بيمين المستأجر لكونه منكراً وجوبها، وإن وقع في المنفقة بدأ بيمين المؤجر، وأيهما نكل لزمه دعوى صاحبه، وأيهما برهن قبل؛ فإن برهنا فبينة المؤجر أولى في الأجرة وبينة المستأجر أولى في المنافع. وإن كان المدة ...
His saying: (And if they differ in the hire contract before utilization, they take mutual oaths) because mutual oath-taking in sale before possession is in accordance with analogy, and hire before utilization is its equivalent. He made it absolute, so it includes the difference in the consideration or the object of hire as in al-Hidaya, and with the fullers as in Munyat al-Mufti, and it does not include when the owner claims the wage and the occupant denies it, and the say is with the hirer (musta'jir). Similarly, if he descends at a caravanserai and they differ, the fatwa is upon the obligation of the wage unless known otherwise; its completion is in al-Bazzaziyya. And in al-Tahdhib: the difference in amount necessitates mutual oaths. End quote. Then if the difference occurs in the rent, the oath begins with the hirer (musta'jir) because he is the denier of its obligation. If the difference occurs in the benefit, the oath begins with the lessor (mu'ajjir). Whichever of them refuses (nukul) is bound by the claim of the other. Whichever provides evidence is accepted. If both provide evidence, then the evidence of the lessor is given precedence in the rents, and the evidence of the hirer is given precedence in the benefits. And if the period...
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage deals with disputes in ijarah (hire) contracts before the service has been utilized. The ruling is that they take mutual oaths, analogizing from sale before possession. The author mentions that this applies to differences in the consideration (rent) or the subject matter (the benefit). There are exceptions: if the owner claims rent and the occupant denies, the word is with the occupant (hirer). Also, in the case of a caravanserai, the default fatwa is that the rent is due unless known otherwise. The passage then details who starts the oath: if the dispute is about the rent amount, the hirer (who denies the obligation) begins; if about the benefit, the lessor (who denies the full benefit was provided) begins. The consequences of refusal (nukul) and evidence are also discussed.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijarah): A contract of hire where one party provides a benefit (e.g., service or use of property) in exchange for rent
استيفاء (istifa'): Utilization or receipt of the benefit in a hire contract
بدل (badal): The consideration in a contract; in ijarah, it is the rent (ujrah)
تحالف (tahalf): Mutual oath-taking between disputing parties, each swearing to their claim

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute over the rent amount in a hire contract before utilization, who begins the oath?
A) The lessor.
B) The hirer.
C) The judge decides.
D) Both take oaths simultaneously.

Key Takeaway
In a hire contract dispute before the benefit is utilized, the Hanafi ruling mandates mutual oaths, with the denier of the claim swearing first.

Ruling on Dispute in Ijarah Before and After Istifa'
Explains when mutual oath applies in lease disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mutual oath in ijarah disputes and apply it to scenarios before and after the tenant has taken benefit.

Core Idea
Mutual oath applies in lease disputes only before the tenant enjoys the property; after enjoyment, the tenant's statement with oath decides the rent.

In lease agreements, disputes over the rent or duration can arise between landlord and tenant. The Hanafi school has a detailed procedure for such disputes based on whether the tenant has already taken benefit (istifa') from the property. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains when mutual oath (tahāluf) is required, the order of oaths, and how partial enjoyment affects the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Ruling
Determine the act under discussion: dispute resolution in ijarah. State the ruling: before istifa', mutual oath is wajib; after istifa', the tenant's statement with oath is taken.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is qiyas to sale before qabd (taking possession). The analogy is based on the subject matter being intact before consumption.
The text states: 'because mutual oath in sale before taking possession is in accordance with analogy, and leasing before enjoyment is its parallel.'
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The common illa is that the subject matter (benefit in ijarah, goods in sale) is not yet consumed. After istifa'/qabd, the subject matter is consumed, preventing mutual oath.
For sale, Muhammad allows mutual oath even after qabd because goods have a value; benefits do not.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad agree that destruction prevents mutual oath in ijarah, but Muhammad had a nuance for sale. The relied-upon position is that after istifa', no mutual oath.
5
Apply to Branches
Consider partial enjoyment: mutual oath applies for the unenjoyed portion, and the tenant's statement governs the past. Also, evidence preference: lessor's evidence for rent, tenant's for benefits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو اختلفا في الإجارة قبل الاستيفاء تحالفا) لأن التحالف في البيع قبل القبض على وفق القياس والإجارة قبل الاستيفاء نظيره أطلقه فشمل الاختلاف في البدل أو المبدل كما في الهداية، ومع القصار كما في منية المفتي ولا يشمل ما إذا ادعى المالك الأجر ونفاه الساكن والقول للمستأجر، وكذا إذا نزل الخان واختلفا والفتوى على وجوب الأجر إلا إذا عرف بخلافه وتمامه في البزازية. وفي التهذيب : الاختلاف في قدر يوجب التحالف اهـ. فإن وقع الاختلاف في الأجرة بدأ بيمين المستأجر لكونه منكراً وجوبها، وإن وقع في المنفقة بدأ بيمين المؤجر، وأيهما نكل لزمه دعوى صاحبه، وأيهما برهن قبل؛ فإن برهنا فبينة المؤجر أولى في الأجرة وبينة المستأجر أولى في المنافع. وإن كان الاختلاف فيهما قبلت بينة كل منهما فيما يدعيه من الفضل نحو أن يدعي هذا شهراً بعشرة والمستأجر شهرين بخمسة فيقضى بشهرين بعشرة. قوله : (وبعده لا والقول قول المستأجر) أي لو اختلفا بعد الاستيفاء فلا تحالف وهذا عندهما ظاهر لأن هلاك المعقود عليه يمنع التحالف عندهما وكذا على أصل محمد لأن الهلاك إنما لا يمنع عنده في المبيع لما أن له قيمة تقوم مقامه فيتحالفان عليها. ولو جرى التحالف ههنا وفسخ العقد فلا قيمة لأن المنافع لا تتقوم بنفسها بل بالعقد، وتبين أنه لا عقد، وإذا امتنع فالقول للمستأجر مع يمينه هو المستحق عليه، ونظير هذه المسألة في التفصيل إجارة الفضولي إن أجازها المالك قبل الاستيفاء فالأجرة له وإن بعده فللعاقد، وإن في بعض المدة فالماضي للعاقد والمستقبل للمالك كما في منية المفتي. قوله : (والبعض معتبر بالكل) يعني لو اختلفا بعد استيفاء البعض تحالفا وفسخ العقد فيما بقي وكان القول في الماضي قول المستأجر لأن العقد ينعقد ساعة فساعة فيصير في كل جزء من المنفعة كأنه ابتداء العقد عليها بخلاف البيع لأن العقد فيه دفعة واحدة، فإذا تعذر في البعض تعذر في الكل. وفي إجارات البزازية المستأجر إن كان هو المدعي فهو يدعي العقد قبل مضي المدة وبعدها، وإن الآجر فهو مدع قبل قبضها وبعد المضي فهو مدعي العين .اهـ. ثم اعلم أن المراد بالاستيفاء التمكن منه في المدة وبعدمه عدمه لما عرف أنه قائم مقامه في وجوب الأجر. ومن فروع التنازع في الإجارة ما في منية المفتي : ادعى اثنان عيناً أحدهما إجارة والآخر شراء فأقر المدعى عليه للمستأجر فلمدعي الشراء أن يحلفه على دعوى الشراء، ولو ادعيا إجارة فأقر لأحدهما ليس للآخر أن يحلفه أجر دابة بعينها من رجل ثم من آخر فأقام الأول بينة، فإن كان الأجر حاضراً تقبل عليه البينة، وإن كان مقراً بما يدعي عليه هذا المدعي وإن كان غائباً لا تقبل اهـ.
His statement: 'And if they differ regarding leasing before enjoyment, they take mutual oaths' because mutual oath in sale before taking possession is in accordance with analogy, and leasing before enjoyment is its parallel. He made it absolute, so it includes difference in the consideration or the object, as in al-Hidaya, and with the fuller (qassar) as in Munyat al-Mufti, and it does not include when the owner claims the rent and the resident denies it; the statement is that of the tenant. Similarly, if he alights at a caravanserai and they differ, the fatwa is on the obligation of rent unless known otherwise; its completion is in al-Bazzaziyya. In al-Tahdhib: difference in amount necessitates mutual oath. If the difference occurs in the rent, the oath begins with the tenant because he is denying its obligation; if in the benefits, it begins with the lessor. Whichever of them declines to swear, the claim of his opponent is binding; whichever presents evidence is accepted; if both present evidence, the lessor's evidence is preferable regarding the rent, and the tenant's evidence is preferable regarding the benefits. If the difference is in both, the evidence of each is accepted regarding what he claims of excess, such as one claims one month for ten and the tenant claims two months for five; judgment is for two months for ten. His statement: 'and after it, no, and the statement is that of the tenant' meaning if they differ after enjoyment, there is no mutual oath. This is apparent according to them (the two shaykhs) because destruction of the subject matter prevents mutual oath according to them, and likewise according to Muhammad's principle, because destruction only does not prevent in the case of sold goods because it has a value that stands in its place, so they take mutual oaths on that. If mutual oath were to occur here and the contract is annulled, there is no value because benefits are not valued in themselves but by the contract, and it becomes clear there is no contract. When it is prevented, the statement is that of the tenant with his oath regarding what is due upon him. The parallel to this issue in detail is the lease by the unauthorized person: if the owner ratifies it before enjoyment, the rent is his; if after, it is for the contractor; if for part of the period, the past is for the contractor and the future for the owner, as in Munyat al-Mufti. His statement: 'and the part is considered with the whole' meaning if they differ after enjoyment of part, they take mutual oaths and the contract is annulled for the remainder, and the statement regarding the past is that of the tenant because the contract is concluded moment by moment, so each part of the benefit is like a separate contract on it, unlike sale because the contract is one lump sum; if it fails in part, it fails entirely. In the Ijarat of al-Bazzaziyya: if the tenant is the claimant, he claims the contract before the passage of time and after; if the lessor is the claimant, he claims before receipt of benefit and after passage of time, so he claims the thing itself. Then know that what is meant by enjoyment is the ability to take benefit during the period; its absence is the opposite, as it is known to stand in place of it regarding the obligation of rent. Among the branches of dispute in lease, as in Munyat al-Mufti: two claim a thing, one by lease and the other by sale; the defendant acknowledges to the tenant, then the claimant of sale can administer an oath regarding the claim of sale. If both claim lease and he acknowledges to one, the other cannot administer an oath. A person hires a specific animal from a man, then from another; the first presents evidence; if the hirer is present, the evidence is accepted against him; if he is absent, it is not accepted.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is the sharh on the matn's ruling regarding disputes in ijarah (lease). The author explains that before the enjoyment (istifa') of the leased property, mutual oath applies, analogous to sale before delivery. The ruling covers disputes over the rent amount or the object. The text details the order of oaths: the tenant begins if the dispute is over the rent (since he denies it), while the lessor begins if the dispute is over the benefits. If one party declines to take the oath, the other's claim is accepted. If both present evidence, the lessor's evidence is preferred for rent, the tenant's for benefits. After enjoyment, however, mutual oath is not allowed because the benefit has been consumed and cannot be returned; the tenant's statement is taken with oath to determine what is due. The commentator also discusses partial enjoyment: if only part was enjoyed, mutual oath applies for the remaining period, and the contract is annulled for the future. The past period is governed by the tenant's statement because each moment of benefit is considered a separate contract. The passage ends with related branches from Munyat al-Mufti, including disputes between a lessee and buyer, and the case of hiring the same animal from two owners.

Key Terms
استيفاء (istīfā'): Enjoyment or taking benefit from the leased property
تحالف (tahāluf): Mutual oath taken by contracting parties when they disagree on terms and lack evidence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a landlord and tenant differ on the rent after the tenant has already lived in the house for the full period, what is the ruling?
A) They take mutual oaths.
B) The landlord's statement is taken with oath.
C) The tenant's statement is taken with oath.
D) The contract is annulled.

Key Takeaway
The timing of the dispute relative to the tenant's enjoyment determines whether mutual oath or the tenant's statement with oath governs the ruling.

Rental Disputes After Utilization: Full vs. Partial
Commentary on the ruling after full and partial utilization in rental disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and apply the Hanafi rule on mutual oath (tahlif) in rental disputes after full and partial utilization, and explain the reasoning based on the nature of benefits (manafi').

Core Idea
After full utilization, no mutual oath; after partial, mutual oath rescinds the remaining contract.

Rental disputes often arise over whether the renter used the property for the entire agreed period. The Hanafi school distinguishes between full utilization (istifa') and partial utilization. This lesson examines the ruling on mutual oath (tahlif) in each case, based on the unique Hanafi view that benefits (manafi') have no independent value outside the contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Recognize when the dispute occurs after full utilization (the entire rental period has passed) or after partial utilization (only part of the period has passed).
This distinction determines the procedure.
2
State the ruling for full utilization
After full utilization, there is no mutual oath (tahlif). The renter's statement is accepted with his oath, as he is the defendant being sued for outstanding rent.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Understand the reasoning for full utilization
Destruction of the subject matter (benefits) prevents oath-taking. Benefits have no independent value outside the contract, so if the contract were rescinded by oath, nothing would remain to be claimed. This differs from a sale where the destroyed item has a market value that can substitute.
Both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad agree on this result, though their principles differ slightly.
4
State the ruling for partial utilization
After partial utilization, the parties take mutual oath. The contract is rescinded for the remaining future period. For the past period already utilized, the renter's statement is accepted with his oath.
The contract is treated as renewed 'moment by moment' (sa'a fa sa'a), each portion separate.
5
Note the analogy and furu'
The commentator gives an analogy with unauthorized lease (ijarat al-fuduli) and cites additional branches (furu') from Munyat al-Mufti and Ijarat al-Bazaziyya, showing how the principles apply in multiple scenarios.
These branches reinforce the core distinction between full and partial utilization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وبعده لا والقول قول المستأجر) أي لو اختلفا بعد الاستيفاء فلا تحالف وهذا عندهما ظاهر لأن هلاك المعقود عليه يمنع التحالف عندهما وكذا على أصل محمد لأن الهلاك إنما لا يمنع عنده في المبيع لما أن له قيمة تقوم مقامه فيتحالفان عليها. ولو جرى التحالف ههنا وفسخ العقد فلا قيمة لأن المنافع لا تتقوم بنفسها بل بالعقد، وتبين أنه لا عقد، وإذا امتنع فالقول للمستأجر مع يمينه هو المستحق عليه، ونظير هذه المسألة في التفصيل إجارة الفضولي إن أجازها المالك قبل الاستيفاء فالأجرة له وإن بعده فللعاقد، وإن في بعض المدة فالماضي للعاقد والمستقبل للمالك كما في منية المفتي قوله : (والبعض معتبر بالكل) يعني لو اختلفا بعد استيفاء البعض تحالفا وفسخ العقد فيما بقي وكان القول في الماضي قول المستأجر لأن العقد ينعقد ساعة فساعة فيصير في كل جزء من المنفعة كأنه ابتداء العقد عليها بخلاف البيع لأن العقد فيه دفعة واحدة، فإذا تعذر في البعض تعذر في الكل. وفي إجارات البزازية المستأجر إن كان هو المدعي فهو يدعي العقد قبل مضي المدة وبعدها، وإن الآجر فهو مدع قبل قبضها وبعد المضي فهو مدعي العين .اهـ. ثم اعلم أن المراد بالاستيفاء التمكن منه في المدة وبعدمه عدمه لما عرف أنه قائم مقامه في وجوب الأجر. ومن فروع التنازع في الإجارة ما في منية المفتي : ادعى اثنان عيناً أحدهما إجارة والآخر شراء فأقر المدعى عليه للمستأجر فلمدعي الشراء أن يحلفه على دعوى الشراء، ولو ادعيا إجارة فأقر لأحدهما ليس للآخر أن يحلفه أجر دابة بعينها من رجل ثم من آخر فأقام الأول بينة، فإن كان الأجر حاضراً تقبل عليه البينة، وإن كان مقراً بما يدعي عليه هذا المدعي وإن كان غائباً لا تقبل اهـ.
His saying: (And after it, no, and the statement is the renter's). That is, if they dispute after utilization, there is no mutual oath. This is apparent according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because destruction of the subject matter prevents oath-taking according to them. Likewise according to Muhammad's principle, because destruction only does not prevent [oath] in a sale because it has a value that substitutes for it, so they take oath over that value. If mutual oath were to occur here and the contract were rescinded, there would be no value because benefits are not independently valuable but by contract, and it becomes clear there is no contract. When it is prevented, the statement is the renter's with his oath, as he is the one against whom claims are made. A parallel to this issue in detail is the unauthorized lease: if the owner ratifies it before utilization, the rent is for him; if after, it is for the contractor; if [ratification occurs] during part of the term, the past portion is for the contractor and the future for the owner, as in Munyat al-Mufti. His saying: (And the part is considered with the whole). That is, if they dispute after utilizing part, they take mutual oath and the contract is rescinded for the remaining period, and the statement regarding the past period is the renter's, because the contract is formed moment by moment, so each portion of benefit is as if a new contract is initiated for it, unlike a sale because the contract is a single unit; if it becomes impossible in part, it is impossible in all. In Ijarat al-Bazaziyya: the renter, if he is the claimant, claims the contract before and after the period; the lessor, if he is the claimant, claims before receiving [the rent] and after the period, he claims the actual object. Then know that what is meant by utilization is the ability to utilize during the period; if not, it is as if not utilized, because it stands in the place of actual utilization in obligating the rent. Among the branches of dispute in rental is what is in Munyat al-Mufti: two people claim an object, one claiming lease, the other purchase; the defendant admits to the renter; then the claimant of purchase can administer an oath to him regarding the claim of purchase. If both claim a lease and he admits to one, the other cannot administer an oath to him. [Example:] a person hired a specific animal from a man, then from another, and the first brought evidence: if the rental fee is present, his evidence is accepted against him; if he is affirming what this claimant claims against him, and if [the fee] is absent, it is not accepted.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the ruling when lessor and lessee dispute after full or partial utilization. The commentator explains that after full utilization (istifa'), no mutual oath (tahlif) takes place. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the destruction of the subject matter prevents oath-taking. According to Imam Muhammad's principle, destruction prevents oath except in sale where the destroyed item has a value that can be substituted, so oath is taken over that value. Here, benefits have no independent value apart from the contract, so if the contract is rescinded by oath, nothing remains to be claimed. Instead, the renter's statement is accepted with his oath, since he is the one being sued for outstanding rent. The commentator provides an analogy: in an unauthorized lease (ijarat al-fuduli), if the owner ratifies before utilization, the rent goes to the owner; if after, to the contractor; if during, the past goes to the contractor and the future to the owner — showing how the point of ratification matters. For partial utilization, the matn says 'the part is considered with the whole,' meaning they take mutual oath and the contract is rescinded for the remaining period. For the past period, the renter's statement is accepted because the rental contract is 'renewed moment by moment' (sa'a fa sa'a), treating each portion of benefit as a separate contract. This differs from a sale, which is one contract; if it fails partially, it fails entirely. The commentary then cites Ijarat al-Bazaziyya on who is the claimant in different scenarios, and Minyat al-Mufti with examples of disputes involving lease and purchase claims. The overall reasoning is based on the distinctive nature of benefits (manafi') as non-corposoreal value that cannot be assigned a separate price after contract nullification.

Key Terms
الاستيفاء (al-istifa'): Complete utilization of the leased benefit for the entire contracted period
التحالف (al-tahlif): Mutual oath-taking between two parties when both deny the contract or its terms and there is no evidence
المنافع (al-manafi'): The usufruct or benefits derived from an object, which in rental are the subject matter of the contract

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a lessor and lessee dispute after the lessee has utilized half the rented period, what is the ruling?
A) No oath is taken; the lessor's statement is accepted.
B) They take mutual oath, the contract is rescinded for the remaining period, and the renter's statement is accepted for the past period.
C) Only the lessor takes an oath; the contract stands.
D) The matter is dismissed; no claim can be made.

Key Takeaway
In rental disputes, the extent of utilization determines the procedure: full utilization avoids mutual oath, while partial utilization triggers mutual oath and rescission for the future, with the renter's testimony preferred for the past.

Definition and Valid Formation of Ijarah
Definition and formation rules of ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ijarah and identify which wordings validly form an ijarah contract.

Core Idea
Ijarah is a sale of benefits; any wording that implies exchange with compensation forms a valid ijarah.

In this lesson, we explore the opening of the Book of Ijarah from al-Bahr al-Raiq. The passage provides the technical definition and then dives into the flexibility of contract formation, emphasizing that the substance (exchange of benefit for wage) matters more than specific words. You will learn how to classify different expressions as valid ijarah or not, and understand the intra-madhhab differences on this issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Definition
Locate the technical definition in the text: 'هي بيع منفعة معلومة بأجر معلوم' (It is the sale of a known benefit for a known wage). Note that ijarah is treated as a type of sale (bay').
The definition establishes the core elements: benefit, wage, and knowledge of both.
2
State the Pillars
The text states: 'وركنها الإيجاب والقبول' (its pillars are offer and acceptance). This is a simple rukn structure; conditions like known benefit/wage are prerequisites, not pillars.
Offer and acceptance can be in any wording that indicates ijarah.
3
Analyze the Wording Flexibility
The passage gives several examples: using the word 'ariyah (lending) with compensation, hibah (gift) of benefits, and even the word of sale (bay') for benefits. For each, determine if it forms a valid ijarah.
The key is presence of compensation ('ajr). Without compensation, it is not ijarah.
4
Note the Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Al-Karkhi initially held that ijarah does not conclude with the word 'sale' (بيع), but later retracted. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it does conclude ijarah. Also, there is a dispute on whether the contract can be attached directly to benefits (without mentioning the object).
The tarjih is based on Shaykh al-Islam's statement and the later view of al-Karkhi.
5
Apply to a Scenario
Given a statement like 'I lend you this book for a month for $10,' classify the contract. According to the text, since compensation is mentioned, it is not 'ariyah but ijarah.
The contract is valid ijarah because the compensation indicates an exchange.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة هي بيع منفعة معلومة بأجر معلوم وما صح ثمنا صح أجرة والمنفعة تعلم ببيان منفعة كتاب الإجارة لما اشتركت الهبة والإجارة في معنى التمليك وكانت الهبة تمليك عين والإجارة تمليك قدم تلك وأخر هذه لكون العين أقوى. وهي في اللغة اسم للأجرة وهي ما يستحق على عمل الخير وتمامه في المغرب. وفي الاصطلاح ما ذكره المصنف. وركنها الإيجاب والقبول، سواء كان بلفظ الإجارة أو بما يدل عليها، فتنعقد بلفظ العارية حتى لو قال لغيره أعرتك هذه الدار شهراً بكذا أو قال كل شهر بكذا وقبل المخاطب كانت الإجارة صحيحة لأنها مأخوذة من التعاور والتداول، وهو كما يكون بغير عوض يكون بعوض، والتعاور بعوض إجارة بخلاف العارية حيث لا تنعقد بلفظ الإجارة حتى لو قال آجرتك هذه الدار بغير عوض كانت إجارة فاسدة ولا تكون عارية لأنها عقد خاص لتمليك المنفعة كما لو قال بعتك هذا العين بغير عوض كان باطلاً أو فاسداً ولا تكون هبة؛ كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان . ولو قال وهبتك منافع هذه الدار شهراً بكذا يجوز وتكون إجارة وفي الفتاوى: لو قال لآخر اشتريت منك خدمة عبدك هذا شهراً بكذا فهي إجارة فاسدة وعن محمد: لو قال أعطيتك هذا العبد ستة يخدمك بكذا جاز وتكون إجارة. وفي المحيط : ولو قال بعت منك منافع الدار شهراً بكذا ذكر في العيون أن الإجارة فاسدة لأن المنافع معدومة وهي ليست بمحل للبيع . وذكر شيخ الإسلام أن فيه اختلاف المشايخ وقال : الحر إذا قال لغيره بعتك نفسي شهراً بكذا لعمل كذا فهو إجارة. وعن الكرخي أن الإجارة لا تنعقد بلفظ البيع ثم رجع وقال : تنعقد . كتاب الإجارة قوله: (ولو قال وهبتك منافع هذه الدار شهراً بكذا يجوز وتكون إجارة) قال الرملي : سيأتي قريباً أنه لو أضيف العقد إلى المنافع لا يجوز اهـ. فتأمله .اهـ. قلت وسيأتي عن المحشي نقل قولين في المسألة فلعل ما هنا على أحدهما.
Book of Ijarah: It is the sale of a known benefit for a known wage. Whatever is valid as a price is valid as a wage. The benefit is known by describing it. The book of Ijarah. Since hibah and ijarah share the meaning of ownership (tamlik), and hibah is ownership of a thing and ijarah is ownership of a benefit, he presented [the former] and delayed [the latter] because the thing is stronger. Lexically, it [ijarah] is the name for the wage which is due for good work and its completion is in al-Mughrib. Technically, it is what the author mentioned. Its pillars are offer and acceptance, whether using the word ijarah or something that indicates it. So it is concluded with the word of 'ariyah. If someone says to another 'I lend you this house for a month for such-and-such' or 'for each month for such-and-such' and the addressee accepts, it is a valid ijarah because it is derived from ta'awur (exchange), which can be for no compensation or with compensation. Exchange with compensation is ijarah, unlike 'ariyah which is not concluded with the word ijarah. If someone says 'I lease you this house without compensation' it is a fasid ijarah, not 'ariyah, because it is a specific contract for ownership of benefit, just as if one says 'I sell you this thing without compensation' it is batil or fasid and not a gift. This in Fatawa Qadikhan. And if he says 'I gift you the benefits of this house for a month for such-and-such' it is valid and it is ijarah. In al-Fatawa: if one says to another 'I bought from you the service of this slave for a month for such-and-such' it is a fasid ijarah. From Muhammad: if he says 'I gave you this slave to serve you for such-and-such' it is valid and is ijarah. In al-Muhit: if he says 'I sold you the benefits of this house for a month for such-and-such' it is mentioned in al-Uyun that the ijarah is fasid because benefits are non-existent and they are not subject to sale. And Shaykh al-Islam said that there is a difference of opinion among the mashayikh. And he said: If a free man says to another 'I sold myself to you for a month for such-and-such work' it is ijarah. From al-Karkhi: ijarah is not concluded with the word of sale, then he retracted and said it is concluded. The author says: (And if he says 'I gift you the benefits of this house for a month for such-and-such' it is valid and is ijarah) al-Ramli said: It will come shortly that if the contract is attached to benefits, it is not valid. So consider it. I say: It will come from al-Muhashi a transmission of two opinions on the issue, so perhaps what is here is one of them.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq opens the Book of Ijarah. It begins with the technical definition: ijarah is the sale of a known benefit for a known wage (هي بيع منفعة معلومة بأجر معلوم). This definition immediately establishes that ijarah is a type of sale (بيع), but specifically of benefits (منافع) rather than physical objects. The author then notes that whatever is valid as a price (ثمن) is valid as a wage (أجرة). The benefit is made known by specifying its details (e.g., duration, type of work). The section then discusses the pillars (ركن) of ijarah: offer (إيجاب) and acceptance (قبول), which can be expressed using the word ijarah or any word that indicates the meaning of ijarah. This is a distinctive Hanafi position that the contract is concluded by any words that convey the intended meaning, not just specific terms. The passage gives several examples: 
- Using the word of 'ariyah (lending) with compensation: if one says 'I lend you this house for a month for such-and-such,' it is a valid ijarah, not 'ariyah, because the compensation makes it a contract of exchange (معاوضة). 
- Using the word of hibah (gift) for benefits: saying 'I gift you the benefits of this house for a month for such-and-such' is valid and considered ijarah. 
- Using the word of sale (بيع) for benefits: there is a difference of opinion. Al-Karkhi initially held that ijarah is not concluded with the word of sale, but later retracted. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to the text is that it does conclude ijarah, as indicated by Shaykh al-Islam's statement. 
- The passage also addresses the case of hiring a free person: if a free man says 'I sold myself to you for a month for such-and-such work,' it is valid ijarah. 
- The text ends with a note from al-Ramli and the author's comment that there is another opinion that if the contract is attached to benefits directly (not to the object), it may not be valid. This indicates a nuance in Hanafi fiqh: the subject matter of ijarah should be benefits attached to an identified object (ayn) or person. 
Overall, the Hanafi school is flexible in the expression of ijarah, focusing on the substance of transferring benefits for compensation, rather than rigid wordings.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijarah): A contract for the sale of a known benefit for a known wage, i.e., a hire or lease agreement.
منفعة (manfa'ah): Benefit, the usufruct or service derived from an object or person, which is the subject matter of ijarah.
أجر (ajr): Wage or rent, the compensation paid for the benefit in an ijarah contract.
عارية (ariyah): Lending without compensation; when combined with compensation, it becomes ijarah.
بيع (bay'): Sale; ijarah is defined as a type of sale of benefits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in al-Bahr al-Raiq, if someone says 'I lend you this house for a month for $500' and the other accepts, what contract is formed?
A) 'Ariyah (gratuitous loan)
B) Ijarah (lease)
C) Hibah (gift)
D) The contract is invalid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, ijarah is a sale of benefits; any wording that implies exchange with compensation forms a valid ijarah, and compensation transforms gratuitous contracts like 'ariyah into ijarah.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate

Definition and Fundamental Rules of Ijarah
Defines Ijarah, its pillars, conditions, and legal basis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ijarah, identify its pillars and conditions, and distinguish between valid and invalid formulations based on the subject matter.

Core Idea
Ijarah is a contract on the physical object; the benefit is owned but not the subject matter.

In this lesson, we explore the foundational definition of ijarah (hiring/leasing) as established in the Hanafi school. The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that ijarah is a 'sale of a known benefit for a known hire', but crucially, the contract itself is on the physical object ('ayn), not the benefit directly. This distinction avoids the problem of contracting on non-existent subject matter and shapes many conditions of validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and its components
Locate the author's definition: 'sale of a known benefit for a known hire'. Note that it is a sale (bay') of the benefit, but the subject matter of the contract is the 'ayn. Also note that anything valid as a price (thaman) is valid as a hire (ujrah).
The definition is both lexical and terminological.
2
Analyze the pillars and permissible wordings
The pillars are offer and acceptance. The contract can be concluded with the word ijarah, or with words like 'ariyah, hibah, or even bay' (with differences of opinion). Understand why ijarah cannot be concluded with the word 'ariyah without compensation.
Focus on the logic: ijarah is derived from exchange, so it works both with and without compensation, but 'ariyah is specifically non-compensatory.
3
Explore the conditions and nullifying factors
Both the benefit and the hire must be known to avoid dispute. The benefit must be maqsudah (intended) from the object. Examples of non-intended benefits render the ijarah void (fasid). Also, long-term ijarah cannot be concluded by mu'atah.
This step covers the practical checks for a valid ijarah.
4
Understand the key distinction: contract on 'ayn vs. on manfa'ah
The passage explains that the contract is actually on the 'ayn by substitution (iqamah al-'ayn maqam al-manfa'ah) because benefits are non-existent at the time of contract. Therefore, adding the contract to benefits directly is invalid. This distinction differentiates the Hanafi definition from al-Quduri's.
This is a critical conceptual point that affects contract wording and validity.

قوله: (ولهذا لو أضاف العقد إلى المنافع لا يجوز قال الرملي : ذكر في البزازية وكثير من الكتب قولين في المسألة قوله : (فهي فاسدة قال الرملي : إنما كانت فاسدة لأنه شرط فيها بيع عين حتى لو وقعت على نفس العين كانت باطلة لا فاسدة بما صرحوا به من أنها لو وقعت على إتلاف
Book of Ijarah. It is the sale of a known benefit for a known hire. And whatever is valid as a price is valid as a hire. The benefit is known by describing the benefit. Since hibah and ijarah share the meaning of ownership, and hibah is ownership of a physical object while ijarah is ownership of a benefit, the former was placed first and the latter later because the physical object is stronger. Lexically, ijarah is a name for the hire, which is what is due for good work; its completion is in al-Mughrib. Terminologically, it is what the author mentioned. Its pillar is offer and acceptance, whether in the word ijarah or in what indicates it. Thus it is concluded with the word ariyah, such that if one said to another 'I lend you this house for a month for such-and-such' or 'for each month for such-and-such' and the addressee accepted, the ijarah is valid because it is derived from ta'awur and tadawul (exchange), and just as it occurs without compensation, it occurs with compensation, and exchange with compensation is ijarah, unlike ariyah, which is not concluded with the word ijarah, such that if one said 'I lease you this house without compensation' it would be a void ijarah and not ariyah because it is a specific contract for ownership of a benefit, just as if one said 'I sell you this physical object without compensation' it would be invalid or void and not a hibah; thus in Fatawa Qadikhan. If one said 'I grant you the benefits of this house for a month for such-and-such' it is permissible and is ijarah. And in al-Fatawa: if one said to another 'I bought from you the service of this slave for a month for such-and-such' it is a void ijarah. And from Muhammad: if one said 'I give you this slave for six months to serve you for such-and-such' it is permissible and is ijarah. And in al-Muhit: if one said 'I sold you the benefits of the house for a month for such-and-such', it is mentioned in al-Uyun that the ijarah is void because benefits are non-existent and are not a proper subject for sale. And Shaykh al-Islam mentioned that there is difference of opinion among the mashayikh, and he said: a free man, if he says to another 'I sold you my soul for a month for such-and-such for such work,' it is ijarah. And from al-Karkhi: ijarah is not concluded with the word bay', then he retracted and said it is concluded. 

Book of Ijarah. His saying: 'If one said I grant you the benefits of this house for a month for such-and-such it is permissible and is ijarah'. Al-Ramli said: It will soon come that if the contract is added to the benefits it is not permissible. End. Reflect on it. End. I say: and it will come from al-Muhashi that there are two opinions in the matter, so perhaps what is here is according to one of them. 

Ijarah for a long term is not concluded by mu'atah (handing over) because the hire is unknown; they may assign a daniq for each year and they may assign a tasuj. For other than long term, ijarah is concluded by mu'atah. All from al-Khulasah from the second chapter on the validity and invalidity of ijarah. Its condition is that the hire and the benefit be known because ignorance of them leads to dispute. Its ruling is that ownership occurs in the two counterparts moment by moment. It is legislated by the Book, which is His saying: 'So if they suckle for you, then give them their hire' (65:6) and others; and the Sunnah: the hadith of Bukhari: 'A man hired a worker, then used him fully but did not give him his hire'; and by consensus. His saying: 'It is the sale of a known benefit for a known hire' means ijarah legally is the ownership of a benefit for a compensation, which excludes sale, hibah, ariyah, and nikah, because the latter is permissibility of benefits for compensation, not ownership of them. 

The author (may Allah have mercy on him) indicated that the contract of ijarah is concluded by the substitution of the physical object in place of the benefit, in terms of the contract's validity, not in terms of ownership. Because a contract must have a subject matter, as it is a condition for validity—the jurists say subject matters are conditions. The subject matter of the contract here is benefits, which are non-existent, and a non-existent thing cannot serve as a subject matter. So the house was made the subject matter by substituting it for the benefits. For this reason, if the contract is added to the benefits, it is not permissible, such as if one says 'I lease you the benefits of this house for a month for such-and-such'. It is only valid when added to the physical object. The meaning of the 'effect' (al-illa) being in effect moment by moment in the words of our mashayikh, according to the occurrence of benefits, is the operation of the 'illa and its penetration into the subject matter moment by moment, not the linking of offer and acceptance every moment, even if the apparent words of our mashayikh suggest that. The ruling is delayed from the time of the contract's effect to the occurrence of benefits moment by moment, because the ruling can be delayed, as in sale with option. Then the contract of ijarah, as established in usul al-fiqh, is an 'illa nominally in that the ruling is attributed to it, and meaningfully in that it is effectual, not a ruling itself due to the delay of the ruling from it; thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. This clarifies that the author's definition is preferable to al-Quduri's definition 'a contract on benefits for compensation' because it has been understood that it is a contract on the physical object, but what is owned is the benefits. What is meant by benefit is the intended benefit from the physical object, such that if one hires clothes to spread them out but not to sit on or sleep, or an animal to tie in his courtyard so that people think it is his, or to make it a mount alongside him, or vessels to place in his house for decoration without using them, or a house not to live in but so that people think he owns it, or a slave not to use him, or dirhams to place them—then in all these the ijarah is void and there is no hire for him; thus in al-Khulasah from the third category on animals. al-Bazzazi explained in his Fatawa that it is a benefit not intended from the physical object. It is mentioned in al-Khulasah in the book of ariyah that if one borrows dirhams to decorate with, it is ariyah not qard, so this indicates that ariyah differs from ijarah in requiring that (the benefit be intended). 

End. 
His saying: 'For this reason if the contract is added to the benefits it is not permissible'. Al-Ramli said: It is mentioned in al-Bazzaziyyah and many books that there are two opinions on the matter. His saying: 'So it is void'. Al-Ramli said: It is only void because it includes a sale of a physical object, so if it occurred on the physical object itself it would be null not void, as they explicitly stated that if it occurs on destruction...
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq opens the Book of Ijarah (hiring/leasing) providing a comprehensive definition and foundational rulings. The author, Ibn Nujaym, follows the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The passage type is a definition with rulings and proofs, expanded by commentary.

1. Definition: Ijarah is defined as 'the sale of a known benefit for a known hire.' This is a legal definition (shar'i). The author notes that anything valid as a price (thaman) is also valid as a hire (ujrah). The benefit is made known by describing it.

2. Lexical and Terminological: Lexically, ijarah is the hire itself. Terminologically, it is as the author defined: a contract for a known benefit in exchange for a known compensation.

3. Pillars: The pillars (rukn) are offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul). This can be in the word ijarah or any word that indicates it. Interestingly, the contract can be concluded with the word 'ariyah (loan) if compensation is mentioned, because ijarah is derived from exchange (ta'awur). However, the reverse does not work: saying 'I lease without compensation' results in a void ijarah, not a valid 'ariyah, because ijarah is a specific contract for ownership of benefit in exchange for compensation.

4. Various wordings: If one says 'I grant you the benefits of this house for a month for such-and-such' it is valid and considered ijarah. If one says 'I bought your slave's service' it is a void ijarah according to the text, but Imam Muhammad allowed 'I give you this slave to serve you for six months for such-and-such.' There is a difference of opinion on using the word bay' (sale) for ijarah. Al-Karkhi initially said it does not conclude ijarah but later retracted.

5. Long-term ijarah: Long-term ijarah is not valid by mu'atah (handing over without verbal offer) because the hire might be unknown (e.g., varying amounts per year). Short-term ijarah can be concluded by mu'atah.

6. Conditions: Both the hire (ujrah) and the benefit (manfa'ah) must be known to avoid dispute.

7. Ruling: Ownership of the two counterparts (benefit and hire) occurs moment by moment as the benefit is realized.

8. Legal basis: The Quran (65:6), Sunnah (hadith of the hired worker from Bukhari), and Ijma' (consensus).

9. Further analysis: The contract is actually on the physical object ('ayn), not on the benefits directly, because benefits are non-existent at the time of contract and cannot be a subject matter. Therefore, the 'ayn is made the subject matter by way of substitution (iqamah al-'ayn maqam al-manfa'ah). If the contract is phrased as 'I lease you the benefits...' it is invalid. This is a critical distinction.

10. Definition preference: The author's definition is better than al-Quduri's ('contract on benefits for compensation') because it correctly identifies the subject matter as the 'ayn while the owned item is the benefit.

11. Benefit must be intended: The benefit must be the intended use of the object. Examples: hiring clothes just to spread them, an animal just to tie for show, vessels for decoration, a house for show of ownership, a slave not to be used, dirhams for display—all these are void because the benefit is not the intended one. This is based on the principle that the benefit must be maqsudah (intended) from the 'ayn.

12. There is a difference of opinion on whether adding the contract to the benefits is invalid or merely void. Some books mention two opinions.

Overall, this passage establishes the essential framework for Ijarah in the Hanafi school, emphasizing the conceptual distinction between the contract's subject matter and what is actually owned.

Key Terms
الإجارة (al-ijarah): A contract of sale of a known benefit for a known hire, where the subject matter is the physical object but the owned item is the benefit.
المنفعة (al-manfa'ah): The benefit that is the intended use of the physical object, known by description and duration.
الأجرة (al-ujrah): The compensation paid for the benefit, which must be known at the time of contract.
العارية (al-'ariyah): A loan of a physical object for use without compensation; the word 'ariyah can be used for ijarah if compensation is mentioned, but ijarah cannot be concluded with the word 'ariyah without compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, on what is the subject matter of the ijarah contract?
A) The benefit (manfa'ah) directly
B) The physical object ('ayn) with the benefit as what is owned
C) Both the physical object and the benefit equally
D) The hire (ujrah)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of ijarah focuses on the physical object as the subject matter, while the benefit is the owned item, a distinction that prevents contracting on non-existent subject matter and shapes conditions of validity.

Long and Short Term Ijarah by Ta'ati
Ruling on validity of ijarah via ta'ati for long vs short terms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when ijarah by ta'ati is valid and explain the condition of wage certainty.

Core Idea
Long-term ijarah requires a known wage; ta'ati is insufficient if wage varies per year.

In Hanafi fiqh, contracts are normally concluded by offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul). However, in some transactions, mutual delivery without formal words (ta'ati) is recognized if the terms are clear from context. This lesson examines when ijarah (hire/lease) can be concluded by ta'ati, based on a ruling from al-Khulasa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its two scenarios
The act is ijarah concluded by ta'ati. The passage distinguishes between long-term (multiple years) and short-term (daily, monthly, etc.).
Ta'ati means mutual handing over of object and wage without formal offer/acceptance.
2
Apply the condition of wage certainty
For ijarah to be valid, the wage must be known (ma'lum) to prevent dispute. In long-term contracts, if the wage per year can differ, total wage becomes uncertain.
The text gives examples: one year a daniq, another a tasuj—different amounts.
3
Derive the ruling for each scenario
Short-term: wage per unit is typically fixed (e.g., daily rate), so wage is known → valid by ta'ati. Long-term: wage may vary per year, unknown → invalid by ta'ati.
The ruling is from al-Khulasa, a later Hanafi fatwa source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تنعقد الإجارة الطويلة بالتعاطي لأن الأجرة غير معلومة قد يجعلون لكل سنة دانقاً وقد يجعلون طسوجاً، وفي غير الطويلة الإجارة تنعقد بالتعاطي، الكل من الخلاصة
And the long-term ijarah is not concluded by ta'ati because the wage is unknown; they might make for each year a daniq and might make a tasuj. For other than long-term, ijarah is concluded by ta'ati. All from al-Khulasa.
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from al-Khulasa regarding the validity of ijarah concluded by ta'ati (mutual delivery without formal offer and acceptance). Long-term ijarah (e.g., for multiple years) is not valid by ta'ati because the total wage is uncertain – they might assign a different amount for each year. Short-term ijarah (e.g., daily or monthly), however, is valid by ta'ati. The underlying reason is that the wage must be known to avoid dispute, and this is more difficult to ensure for long periods.

Key Terms
التعاطي (al-ta'āṭī): A contract concluded by mutual handing over of the object and price without formal verbal offer and acceptance.
دانق (dāniq): A small silver coin, one-sixth of a dirham.
طسوج (ṭasūj): A small weight or coin, one-twenty-fourth of a dirham.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is long-term ijarah not concluded by ta'ati?
A) Because ta'ati is only valid for sales
B) Because the wage is uncertain and may vary per year
C) Because ijarah always requires a court
D) Because the Hanafi school rejects all contracts by ta'ati

Key Takeaway
Ijarah by ta'ati is valid for short-term contracts where the wage is known, but invalid for long-term if the wage is uncertain.

The Definition and Proofs of Ijarah in Hanafi Fiqh
Defines ijarah and provides proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ijarah, identify its essential condition, and cite the primary textual proofs.

Core Idea
Ijarah is a sale of usufruct – ownership of benefit transferred for wage, not mere permissibility.

This lesson unpacks the classical Hanafi definition of ijarah (lease/hire) from Ibn Nujaym's Al-Bahr al-Raiq. You will learn how the Hanafi school defines ijarah as tamlik al-manfa'ah (transfer of ownership of benefit), its essential condition of known wage and benefit, and the Quranic, Hadith, and Ijma' proofs that establish its legitimacy. We also clarify what ijarah is NOT – distinguishing it from sale, gift, loan, and marriage.

Guided Path
1
Extract the definition
The text states: 'الإجارة شرعاً تمليك منفعة بعوض'. Identify the three components: تمليك (transfer of ownership), منفعة (usufruct), بعوض (for compensation). Note that the Hanafi definition emphasizes transfer of ownership, distinguishing it from mere permissibility.
The word تمليك is key – it implies ownership passes to the lessee.
2
Identify the essential condition
Both the wage (أجرة) and the benefit (منفعة) must be known (معلومتين) at the time of contract. Ignorance leads to dispute, which invalidates the contract.
This condition is shared by all sales (bay').
3
Trace the proofs
Three proofs are cited: (1) Quran Surah At-Talaq 65:6 commands giving wages to nursing mothers; (2) Sunnah – the hadith in Bukhari about a hired worker whose wage was withheld; (3) Ijma' – consensus of scholars on the permissibility of ijarah.
The imperative 'فآتوهن' indicates obligation to pay, supporting the validity of wage-based contracts.
4
Apply the definition to exclude other contracts
The text explicitly excludes sale (bay'), gift (hibah), loan ('ariyah), and marriage (nikah). Sale transfers an 'ayn (tangible object), not a benefit; gift and loan are gratuitous; marriage gives ibahah (permissibility to enjoy) without transferring ownership of the benefit.
Understanding these exclusions sharpens the precise boundaries of ijarah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من الفصل الثاني في صحة الإجارة وفسادها وشرطها أن تكون الأجرة والمنفعة معلومتين لأن جهالتهما تفضي إلى المنازعة وحكمها وقوع الملك في البدلين ساعة فساعة وهي مشروعة بالكتاب وهو قوله تعالى فإن أرضعن لكم فآتوهن أجورهن :[الطلاق: ٦] وغيره. والسنة حديث البخاري ورجل استأجر أجيراً فاستوفى منه ولم يعطه أجره والإجماع قوله : (هي) بيع معلومة بأجر معلوم يعني الإجارة شرعاً تمليك منفعة بعوض فخرج البيع والهبة والعارية والنكاح فإنه استباحة المنافع بعوض لا تمليكها
From the second chapter on the validity and invalidity of ijarah and its condition that the wage and the benefit must be known because their ignorance leads to dispute. And its ruling is that ownership of the two exchanges occurs moment by moment. And it is legislated by the Book: His statement 'So if they nurse for you, then give them their wages' [At-Talaq:6] and others; and the Sunnah: the hadith of Bukhari about a man who hired a worker, received the work from him, and did not give him his wage; and consensus. His statement: (It) is a sale of a known thing for a known wage, meaning ijarah in Islamic law is the transfer of ownership of a usufruct for compensation, so sale, gift, loan, and marriage are excluded, for marriage is a permissibility of usufructs for compensation, not their transfer.
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage from the introduction of the chapter on ijarah first states the essential condition: both the wage (ujrah) and the benefit (manfa'ah) must be known to avoid dispute. The ruling is that ownership of the countervalues passes progressively as the benefit is realized. Then three proofs are cited: (1) Quran: verse 6 of Surah At-Talaq commands giving wages to nursing mothers; (2) Sunnah: the hadith in Bukhari warns against withholding an employee's wage; (3) Ijma': consensus of scholars on the permissibility of ijarah. The author then defines ijarah as a 'sale of a known thing for a known wage' and explains it as the transfer of ownership of a usufruct for a compensation. This definition excludes sale (transfer of an 'ayn), gift and loan (gratuitous), and marriage (which only permits but does not transfer ownership of usufructs).

Key Terms
الإجارة (al-ijārah): Transfer of ownership of a usufruct in exchange for a known wage, akin to a sale of a known benefit.
المنفعة (al-manfa'ah): The lawful, intended benefit from an asset, such as residence, riding, or services.
بدلين (badalayn): The two exchanges in ijarah: the wage and the benefit, ownership of which passes progressively.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is excluded from the definition of ijarah?
A) Sale (bay')
B) Loan ('ariyah)
C) Marriage (nikah)
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Ijarah in Hanafi fiqh is defined as the transfer of ownership of a usufruct for a known wage, validated by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma', and its validity hinges on the knowledge of both wage and benefit.
