Specifying Benefit in Hire by Naming the Work: Conditions for Validity
Expansion of the ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq on specifying benefit in hire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid hire contract when the benefit is specified by naming the work, and distinguish between the requirements for a common worker (ajir mushtarak) and a private worker (ajir wahid).

Core Idea
In a hire contract, naming the work is necessary but not sufficient; additional details (object, attributes, time/place) must be known to avoid invalidity.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expounds a key principle of ijara: the benefit can be known by naming the type of work, such as dyeing or sewing. However, simply stating the work is insufficient; the specific object, its attributes, and for certain contracts, the time or place must also be specified. We will examine these conditions and their application to different types of workers and scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of workers
Distinguish between al-ajir al-mushtarak (common worker, hired for a specific task) and al-ajir al-wahid (private worker, hired for a period). The passage states that for the common worker, the work must be known; for the private worker, time must be specified.
This distinction is fundamental in Hanafi ijara.
2
List the requirements for naming the work
For a common worker, naming the work (e.g., dyeing) is a starting point, but further specification is needed: the object (the garment), its attributes (color, quantity if variable), and for other tasks like sewing, the garment must be known. For riding animals, time or place must be specified.
The passage cites examples from al-Hidayah and Tuhfat al-Fuqaha.
3
Apply the conditions to specific cases
Work through the examples: dyeing requires specifying the garment, color, and quantity; sewing requires a known garment; hiring an animal for riding requires time or place; hiring a washerman (common worker) requires the work to be known (e.g., number of garments).
Failure to specify renders the contract fasid (invalid).
4
Note the consequence of missing specification
If any required specification is omitted, the hire is invalid (fasid). The passage applies this to contemporary practice, noting that hire of animals by fodder sellers (without time/place) is invalid.
This shows the ongoing relevance of these principles.
5
Distinguish from other types of specification
For a private worker (ajir wahid), time is the key specification; for a common worker, the task itself must be clearly defined. The passage notes that some sources treat the private worker as a subtype of 'work hire' but still require time specification.
This nuance appears in Tuhfat al-Fuqaha and Ghayat al-Bayan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو) بالتسمية كالاستئجار على صبغ الثوب وخياطته) يعني تعرف المنفعة بالتسمية كالصبغ ونحوه، ومنه استئجار الدابة للحمل أو للركوب والإجارة على العمل كاستئجار القصار ونحوه، ولا بد أن يكون العمل معلوماً وذلك في الأجير المشترك، وأما الأجير الواحد فمن النوع الأوّل، ولا بد فيه من بيان الوقت؛ كذا في الهداية. وصرح في تحفة الفقهاء بأنه من نوع الاستئجار على العمل لكن لا بد فيه من بيان الوقت واختاره في غاية البيان. وأشار بقوله على صبغ الثوب» إلى أنه لا بد أن يعين الثوب الذي يصبغ، ولون الصبغ بأنه أحمر أو نحوه، وقدر الصبغ إذا كان مما يختلف. وأشار بقوله «وخياطته» إلى أنه لا بد أن يكون الثوب معلوماً ولهذا قال في المحيط : لو استأجره لقصر عشرة أثواب ولم يرها فالإجارة فاسدة وإن سمى جنسها لأنه يختلف بغلظه ورقته واعلم أن استئجار الدابة للركوب لا بد فيه من بيان الوقت أو الموضع حتى لو خلا عنهما فهي فاسدة، ذكره البزازي في فتاواه. وبه يعلم فساد إجارة دواب العلافين الواقعة في زماننا لعدم بيان الوقت والموضع .
His statement: 'Or by naming, like leasing for dyeing a garment and sewing it' means that the benefit is known by naming, like dyeing and similar. From this is leasing a riding animal for carrying or riding, and hire for work like hiring a washerman and similar. It is necessary that the work be known, and that is in the case of a common worker (ajir mushtarak). As for a private worker (ajir wahid), it falls under the first type, and it requires specifying the time; thus in al-Hidaya. And it is stated explicitly in Tuhfat al-Fuqaha that it is of the type of hire for work, but it requires specifying the time, and he chose this in Ghayat al-Bayan. And he indicated by his statement 'on dyeing a garment' that it is necessary to specify the garment to be dyed, the color (red or similar), and the quantity if it varies. And by his statement 'and sewing it' he indicated that the garment must be known. For this reason, it is said in al-Muhit: If someone hired him to shorten ten garments and did not see them, the hire is invalid even if he specified the type, because it differs in thickness and thinness. And know that hiring an animal for riding requires specifying the time or place; if both are omitted, it is invalid, mentioned by al-Bazzazi in his fatawa. And by this the invalidity of the hire of animals of fodder sellers in our time is known, due to not specifying the time and place.
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage explains how the benefit in a hire contract can be known by naming the work, such as dyeing a cloth or sewing. There are two types: a common worker (ajir mushtarak) is hired for a specific task, and the task must be clearly specified; a private worker (ajir wahid) is hired for a period, and the time must be specified. The passage gives examples: for dyeing, one must specify the cloth, color, and quantity if it varies. For sewing, the garment must be known. For riding an animal, the time or place must be mentioned. Failure to specify leads to invalidity. The author applies this to contemporary practice, finding that hire of animals in 'allafin' (fodder sellers) is invalid due to lack of time and place.

Key Terms
الأجير المشترك (al-ajir al-mushtarak): A worker who works for many people; his hire is for a specific task, not a specific time.
الأجير الواحد (al-ajir al-wahid): A private worker hired exclusively for a period; his hire requires specification of time.
صبغ الثوب (sabh al-thawb): Dyeing the garment; an example of benefit known by naming.
خياطة (khiyatah): Sewing; another example of benefit known by naming.
استئجار الدابة للركوب (isti'jar al-dabbah li al-rukub): Hiring an animal for riding; requires specifying the time or place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required for a valid hire contract to dye a garment?
A) Only naming the work 'dyeing' is sufficient.
B) Specifying the garment, the color, and the quantity if it varies.
C) Specifying the time only.
D) Specifying the place of work.

Key Takeaway
In a hire contract, the benefit must be known; naming the work is necessary but must be accompanied by specifying the object, its relevant attributes, and for certain contracts, the time or place, to avoid invalidity.

Leasing Waqf Property Below Market Rent and Price Changes
Ruling on waqf lease below market rate with price change scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a waqf property is leased below market rent and explain the conditions under which the lease is rescinded due to price changes.

Core Idea
A lease of waqf property below market rate obliges the lessee to pay the fair market rent, and price increases may rescind the contract.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a critical issue in waqf management: when a trustee leases waqf property below the fair market rent. The Hanafi position, as preferred by later scholars, holds that the lessee must pay the full fair market rent (ujr al-mithl) to protect the waqf's interests. Additionally, the passage outlines how price fluctuations affect the lease's validity, including situations where the lease cannot be immediately rescinded due to an existing crop.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the legal act being examined? Leasing waqf property for a rent that is significantly below the market rate (ujr al-mithl). The ruling is that the lessee is obliged to pay the full ujr al-mithl, not just the named rent.
This is the mufta bihi position according to later Hanafi scholars.
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
The text cites 'some of our scholars' and states 'the fatwa is upon it.' It also references al-Dhakhirah, al-Asbijabi, Qadi Khan, and al-Allama Qasim. The proof is based on the principle that the lease was invalid due to excessive undervaluation (ghabn fahish), and the waqf must be protected.
No explicit Quran or hadith is quoted; the dalil is the established need to preserve waqf assets.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof supports the ruling)
The lease is considered void from the start because the rent was less than an amount people would overlook (لا يتغابن الناس). Therefore, the lessee's possession is without valid contract, and he must pay the market rate. This is analogous to a defective sale where the price is unknown.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The ruling is attributed to 'some of our scholars' (ba'd 'ulama'ina), implying earlier scholars may have held the lease valid at the named rent. The later preferred view (mufta bihi) is to require ujr al-mithl to safeguard the waqf.
The ikhtilaf is between earlier and later authorities.
5
Evaluate the tarjih authority
Al-Allama Qasim in his Fatawa preferred the view requiring ujr al-mithl because it is 'more beneficial for the waqf' (أنفع للوقف). This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
The authority weight is fatawa mutakhkhirin (later fatwa collections).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومتولي الوقف أجرها بغير أجر المثل يلزم مستأجرها تمام أجر المثل عند بعض علمائنا وعليه الفتوى ا هـ. وقال في الذخيرة : وإذا أجر القيم داراً بأقل من أجر المثل قدر ما لا يتغابن الناس حتى لم تجز الإجارة لو تسلمها المستأجر كان عليه أجر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ على ما أجازه المتأخرون من المشايخ ا هـ. وذكر الأسبيجابي في المزارعة إذا كانت الأرض أرض وقف استأجرها من المتولي إلى طويل المدة ينظر ؛ إن كان السعر بحاله لم يزدد ولم ينقص كما كان وقت العقد فإنه يجوز . وإن غلا أجر مثلها فإنه يفسخ ذلك العقد ويحتاج إلى تجديد ذلك العقد ثانياً، وكذلك إذا استأجرها بأجرة معلومة إلى سنة فلما مضى نصف السنة غلا سعرها وازداد أجر مثلها فإنه يفسخ ذلك العقد ويعقد ثانياً على أجرة معلومة ولو كانت الأرض بحال لم يمكن فسخها نحو ما إذا كان فيها زرع لم يحصد بعد ولم يدرك بعد فلا يمكن فسخها ولكن إلى وقت زيادته يجب المسمى بقدره وبعد الزيادة إلى تمام السنة يجب أجر مثلها. وأما إذا كان ينتقص من أجرتها يعني رخص أجرتها وسعرها قبل مضي المدة فإن الإجارة لا تبطل ولا لأن المستأجر قد رضي بذلك حيث عقد عليها وزيادة الأجرة إنما تعتبر إذا زادت عند الكل، فأما إذا زاد واحد في أجرتها تعنتاً على المستأجر الأول فلا يعتبر ذلك ولا يبطل العقد ولا يفسخ ما لم تمض المدة، وكذلك حكم الحانوت والطاحونة وجميع ما يكون وقفاً استؤجر من المتولي ا.هـ. وكذا ذكر قاضيخان في فتاواه ورجحه العلامة قاسم في فتاواه بأنه أنفع للوقف
The trustee of a waqf leased it for less than the fair rent; the lessee is obliged (to pay) the full fair rent according to some of our scholars, and the fatwa is upon it. And it is said in al-Dhakhirah: If the guardian leased a house for less than the fair rent by an amount that people would not overlook, such that the lease was not valid, if the lessee had taken possession, he must pay the fair rent, no matter how high, according to what the later scholars (mutakhkhirun) have approved. And al-Asbijabi mentioned in al-Muzara'ah: If the land is waqf land and someone leased it from the trustee for a long period, it is considered: if the price remains as it was at the time of the contract without increase or decrease, then it is permissible. But if the rent increased, the contract is rescinded and needs to be renewed. Similarly, if he leased it for a known rent for a year, then after half the year the rent went up, the contract is rescinded and a new contract made at the new known rent. But if the land cannot be rescinded, e.g., if there is a crop not yet harvested, then until the increase time, the named rent is due for its portion, and after the increase until the end of the year, the fair rent is due. If the rent decreases before the term ends, the lease is not invalidated because the lessee was satisfied with that when he contracted. Increase is only considered if the rent increases for everyone; if one person arbitrarily increases it to bother the first lessee, it is not considered and does not invalidate the contract. The same ruling applies to shops, mills, and all waqf property leased from the trustee. And Qadi Khan mentioned in his Fatawa, and al-Allama Qasim preferred in his Fatawa that it is more beneficial for the waqf.
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when a waqf property is leased below the market rate. It begins by stating the position of some Hanafi scholars that the lessee must pay the full fair rent, and this is the relied-upon position. The commentary from al-Dhakhirah reinforces that the guardian must ensure the rent is not significantly below market, and if it is, the lessee must pay the market rate regardless. The discussion from al-Asbijabi focuses on long-term leases of waqf land: if the rent remains stable, the lease is valid; if it increases, the original contract is rescinded and a new one must be made at the higher rate. However, if there is a crop preventing termination, the lessee pays the named rent until harvest and then the fair rent from that point. If the rent decreases, the lease remains valid because the lessee agreed to it. An arbitrary increase by one party to harass the lessee is not considered. The same rule applies to all waqf properties. Qadi Khan and al-Allama Qasim confirm this ruling as more beneficial for the waqf.

Key Terms
أجر المثل (ujr al-mithl): The fair market rent for the property at the time of lease.
غبن فاحش (ghabn fahish): Excessive undervaluation – an amount that people would not overlook, rendering the transaction invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a waqf property is leased significantly below the fair market rent and the lessee has taken possession, what does the relied-upon Hanafi position oblige the lessee to pay?
A) The named rent only.
B) The difference between named rent and fair rent.
C) The full fair market rent.
D) None; the lease is void and the lessee must vacate.

Key Takeaway
The lease of waqf property below market rate obliges the lessee to pay the fair market rent, and the lease may be rescinded if the market rent increases, subject to exceptions.

Defining Benefit by Description (Tasmia) in Ijarah
Explanation of how benefit is specified by description with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the requirements for specifying benefit by description in an ijarah contract and apply them to distinguish valid from invalid contracts.

Core Idea
Benefit in ijarah must be known; description requires specifying details like item, color, quantity, time, or place.

This passage expands on the second method of defining benefit in ijarah: tasmia (description). The commentator uses examples from dyeing, sewing, and animal hire to show the precise conditions required. Understanding these details is crucial for drafting valid contracts and avoiding disputes over wages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of workers
The passage distinguishes between ajir mushtarak (shared worker) and ajir wahid (exclusive worker). Note how specification requirements differ for each.
Ajir mushtarak: work must be known in detail. Ajir wahid: time must be specified.
2
List specifications for ajir mushtarak
From the dyeing example, extract the required details: the garment itself, the color of dye, and the quantity if it varies. These make the benefit known.
General principle: any detail that affects the value must be specified.
3
Note additional requirement for ajir wahid
For exclusive workers hired by time, the time period must be specified. This is emphasized from al-Hidayah and Tuhfat al-Fuqaha.
Even if the work type is known, without time the contract can be fasid.
4
Apply to animal hire
Hiring an animal for riding requires specifying either the time or the place. Omitting both invalidates the contract.
The passage cites al-Bazzazi and applies this to contemporary stable hire.
5
Reflect on contemporary practice
The commentator notes that common practice of hiring horses without time/place is invalid. This shows the timeless relevance of these conditions.
Always check if the contract's benefit is sufficiently defined.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو) بالتسمية كالاستئجار على صبغ الثوب وخياطته) يعني تعرف المنفعة بالتسمية كالصبغ ونحوه، ومنه استئجار الدابة للحمل أو للركوب والإجارة على العمل كاستئجار القصار ونحوه، ولا بد أن يكون العمل معلوماً وذلك في الأجير المشترك، وأما الأجير الواحد فمن النوع الأوّل، ولا بد فيه من بيان الوقت؛ كذا في الهداية. وصرح في تحفة الفقهاء بأنه من نوع الاستئجار على العمل لكن لا بد فيه من بيان الوقت واختاره في غاية البيان. وأشار بقوله على صبغ الثوب» إلى أنه لا بد أن يعين الثوب الذي يصبغ، ولون الصبغ بأنه أحمر أو نحوه، وقدر الصبغ إذا كان مما يختلف. وأشار بقوله «وخياطته» إلى أنه لا بد أن يكون الثوب معلوماً ولهذا قال في المحيط : لو استأجره لقصر عشرة أثواب ولم يرها فالإجارة فاسدة وإن سمى جنسها لأنه يختلف بغلظه ورقته واعلم أن استئجار الدابة للركوب لا بد فيه من بيان الوقت أو الموضع حتى لو خلا عنهما فهي فاسدة، ذكره البزازي في فتاواه. وبه يعلم فساد إجارة دواب العلافين الواقعة في زماننا لعدم بيان الوقت والموضع
His saying: 'Or by description (tasmia), such as hiring for dyeing a garment and sewing it' means benefit is known by description such as dyeing and the like. Included is hiring an animal for carrying or riding, and hiring for work like hiring a washerman, etc. The work must be known, and that is for the shared worker (ajir mushtarak). As for the exclusive worker (ajir wahid), it falls under the first type, and it is necessary to specify the time; thus in al-Hidayah. It is stated in Tuhfat al-Fuqaha that it is of the type of hiring for work, but it is necessary to specify the time, and that is chosen in Ghayat al-Bayan. His saying 'on dyeing the garment' indicates that it is necessary to specify the garment to be dyed, the color of the dye, and the amount of dye if it varies. His saying 'and its sewing' indicates the garment must be known. Hence in al-Muhit: If one hires a washerman for ten garments without seeing them, the lease is invalid even if he specifies the type, because it varies in thickness and thinness. Know that hiring an animal for riding requires specifying the time or place; if both are omitted, the lease is invalid. This is mentioned by al-Bazzazi in his Fatawa. From this, one knows the invalidity of the common practice of hiring horses from the stable owners today, due to not specifying time and place.
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage explains the second method of defining benefit in an ijarah contract: by description (tasmia). The commentator expands on the matn's mention of dyeing and sewing as examples. For benefit to be known, the work must be clearly specified. For a shared worker (ajir mushtarak), the work and its details must be known, including the specific item (e.g., the cloth), the color, and the quantity if it affects the value. For a dedicated worker (ajir wahid), the time must also be specified. The passage cites al-Hidayah and Tuhfat al-Fuqaha to stress the need for time specification in such contracts. It further references al-Muhit to show that hiring a washerman for unseen garments is invalid because garments vary in quality. For animal hire, both time and place must be stated; common practice of hiring horses from stable owners without these details is invalid.

Key Terms
الأجير المشترك (ajir mushtarak): A worker hired by multiple people or for multiple tasks, not exclusively for one person.
الأجير الواحد (ajir wahid): An exclusive worker hired by one person for a specific period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) The number of riders.
D) The type of saddle.

Key Takeaway
Benefit in ijarah must be made known; when defined by description, every detail that affects the value must be specified, otherwise the contract is invalid.

Defining Benefit by Pointing in Ijarah
Expansion of pointing as a valid method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that pointing (ishara) is a valid method of defining benefit in ijarah contracts and apply it to determine contract validity.

Core Idea
Pointing to the object and destination in ijarah makes the benefit known, rendering the contract valid.

In ijarah (hire/lease), the benefit (manfa'ah) must be known for the contract to be valid. While description (sifah) is common, what happens when the item is physically present but cannot be fully described? The Hanafi school recognises pointing (ishara) as a valid alternative, as explained in this passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the method
Recognise that the text introduces pointing (ishara) as the third method of defining benefit, after description and showing.
This applies when the object is physically present.
2
Understand the condition
For pointing to be valid, the object and its destination must both be clearly indicated. The text mentions 'this food' and 'this place'.
Ambiguous pointing invalidates the contract.
3
Apply to a scenario
Given a scenario, determine if the contract is valid when only pointing is used. If the object is present and destination is clear, the contract is valid.
Contrast with description: pointing is used when the benefit cannot be adequately described.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو بالإشارة كالاستئجار على نقل هذا الطعام إلى كذا) يعني تعرف المنفعة بالإشارة لأنه إذا أراه ما ينقله والموضع الذي يحمل إليه كانت المنفعة معلومة فيصح العقد
His saying: 'Or by pointing, such as hiring for transporting this food to such place' means benefit is known by pointing, because when he shows him the thing he is to transport and the place to which it is to be carried, the benefit becomes known, so the contract is valid.

Commentary
The commentator explains the third method of defining benefit in an ijarah contract: by pointing (ishara). When the subject matter is physically present, the lessor can point to the item to be transported (e.g., this food) and the destination (e.g., this place). This makes the benefit known, and the contract is valid. This method is used when the benefit cannot be easily described, such as when the quantity or quality is variable and the actual item is available to point at.

When Rent Becomes Owned: The Four Means in Ijarah
Ruling on the ownership of rent with four ways and intra-Hanafi dispute on ibra'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four means by which rent becomes owned in Hanafi fiqh and apply them to determine the lessor's entitlement.

Core Idea
Rent is not owned by contract alone; it becomes owned only through advance payment, condition, receipt, or ability to use.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a pivotal Hanafi distinction: the rent (ujra) in an ijarah contract is not a debt owed immediately upon signing, unlike the price in a sale. Instead, the lessor becomes entitled to the rent only after one of four specific events occurs. Understanding this framework is essential for determining when the lessor can demand payment, detain the property, or rescind the contract.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its scope
The rent is not owned by the contract itself. This means the lessor does not acquire a right to the rent merely by concluding the ijarah contract.
The contract is valid (sahih), but the rent remains a future obligation until one of the four events triggers ownership.
2
Identify the four means of ownership
The rent becomes owned by: (1) ta'jeel (advance payment), (2) shart (condition in the contract stipulating immediate payment), (3) istifa' (actual receipt of the benefit by the lessee), or (4) tamakkun (the lessor delivering the property so the lessee can use it).
These are the sole ways the lessor becomes entitled to the rent.
3
Explore tamakkun and its practical implications
Tamakkun means the lessor puts the lessee in a position to use the property without hindrance. If delivery occurs after the lease period, the lessee may have a choice to accept the remainder, especially if the lease was for a specific season.
Delivery of the key in a city constitutes tamakkun; in the countryside, it does not unless the lessee actually arrives.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on ibra'
The text notes a disagreement between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf: Muhammad holds that ibra' (discharge) from the rent is valid even before ownership, while Abu Yusuf disagrees.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Muhammad's view.
5
Apply to a practical scenario
Consider a lessee who pays rent in advance (ta'jeel). The rent is owned immediately; the lessor can demand it, but cannot sell the debt before receipt. If the lessee defaults, the lessor may detain the property.
The lessor cannot sell the rent before it is owned, as it is not yet a secured debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والأجرة لا تملك بالعقد بل بالتعجيل أو بشرطه أو بالاستيفاء أو بالتمكن) يعني لا يملك الأجرة إلا بواحد من هذه الأربعة والمراد أنه لا يستحقها المؤجر إلا بذلك كما أشار إليه القدوري في مختصره لأنها لو كانت ديناً لا يقال إنه ملكه المؤجر قبل قبضه، وإذا استحقها المؤجر قبل قبضها فله المطالبة بها وحبس المستأجر عليها وحبس العين عنه وله حق الفسخ إن لم يعجل له المستأجر ؛ كذا في المحيط. لكن ليس له بيعها قبل قبضها. وأشار المصنف رحمه الله تعالى إلى أن المستأجر لو باع المؤجر بالأجر شيئاً وسلم جاز لتضمنه اشتراط التعجيل فتقع المقاصة بينهما، فإن تعذر إيفاء العمل رجع بالدراهم دون المتاع. والمراد من التمكن تسليم المحل إلى المستأجر بحيث لا مانع من الانتفاع ، فلو سلمه بعد مضي المدة فليس لأحدهما الامتناع من التسليم والتسلم في الباقي إذا لم يكن في مدة الإجارة وقت يرغب في الإجارة لأجله، فإن كان في المدة وقت كذلك كحانوت يستأجر سنة لرواج السوق في بعضها أو دار بمكة تستأجر سنة لأجل الموسم فلم يسلم في الوقت الذي يرغب لأجله فإنه يتخير في قبض الباقي كما في البيع. وفي الذخيرة من الفصل السابع والعشرين في الاختلاف : لو اختلف المستأجر والآجر بعد شهر والمفتاح مع المستأجر وقال لم أقدر على فتحه وقال المؤجر بل قدرت على فتحه وسكنت ولا بينة لهما يحكم الحال، وإن أقاماها فالبينة لرب المنزل لأنه لا عبرة لتحكيم الحال متى جاءت البينة بخلافه. وفي القنية : تسليم المفتاح في التخلية بينه وبين الدار تسليم للدار حتى يجب الأجر بمضي المدة وإن لم يسكن، وتسليم المفتاح في السواد ليس بتسليم الدار وإن حضر المصر والمفتاح في يده ا هـ
His saying: 'And the rent is not owned by the contract, but by advance payment (ta'jeel), or by condition (shart), or by receipt (istifa'), or by ability (tamakkun).' That is, the rent is not owned except by one of these four. It means that the lessor is not entitled to it except thereby, as al-Quduri indicated in his Mukhtasar. If it were a debt, it would not be said that the lessor owned it before receipt. When the lessor becomes entitled to the rent before receipt, he has the right to demand it, to detain the lessee for it, to retain the property from the lessee, and to rescind if the lessee does not pay promptly; thus in al-Muhit. But he may not sell it before receipt. And the author indicated that if the lessee sells something to the lessor for the rent and delivers, it is valid because it implies a condition of advance payment, resulting in set-off. If the work cannot be performed, he recovers the money, not the goods. The meaning of tamakkun is delivering the place to the lessee such that there is no hindrance to use. If he delivers after the period has passed, neither party may refuse to deliver and receive for the remaining time if there is no time in the lease period that is desirable for the purpose. If there is such a time, like a shop rented for a year with a favorable market season, or a house in Mecca rented for the season, and it was not delivered at the desirable time, then the lessee may choose whether to receive the remainder, as in sale. In al-Dhakhirah, in the twenty-seventh chapter on disputes: If the lessee and lessor dispute after a month, with the key in the lessee's hand, and the lessee says he could not open it, and the lessor says he did open it and lived there, and there is no evidence, the current state (handing) is decisive. If both present evidence, the lessor's evidence is preferred because the current state is not considered when evidence contradicts it. In al-Qunya: Delivering the key to vacate the house constitutes delivery of the house such that rent becomes due with the passage of time even if he does not live there. But delivering the key in the countryside is not delivery of the house even if he arrives at the city and the key is in his hand, end.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage examines the nature of the rent (ujr) in an ijarah contract. The matn states that the rent is not owned by the contract itself, unlike the price in a sale. Instead, ownership (and thus entitlement) of the rent occurs through one of four events: (1) ta'jeel: the lessee actually pays the rent in advance, (2) shart: the contract includes a condition that the rent is due immediately (such as upon signing), (3) istifa': the lessee actually receives the benefit (e.g., uses the property), or (4) tamakkun: the lessor delivers the property so that the lessee can use it, even if the lessee does not actually use it. The lessor cannot sell the rent before it is owned (i.e., before one of these events). The passage also discusses the effect of tamakkun: if delivery is delayed until after the period, the lessee may have a choice whether to accept the remainder, especially if there was a particular season for which the lease was intended. A dispute scenario is given: if the lessor and lessee disagree about whether the lessee was able to use the property (key in hand), the current state (hand) is evidence; but if both bring witnesses, the lessor's testimony is preferred because the apparent state does not override clear evidence. Finally, it distinguishes between delivering the key in the city (which constitutes delivery of the house) and in the countryside (which does not unless the lessee actually comes to the city).

Key Terms
الأجرة (al-ujra): The rent or wage in an ijarah contract.
التعجيل (al-ta'jeel): Advance payment of the rent before receiving the benefit.
الشرط (al-shart): A condition in the contract that the rent is due immediately.
الاستيفاء (al-istifa'): Actual receipt of the benefit (using the leased property).
التمكن (al-tamakkun): The ability to use the property after delivery, even if not used.
الإبراء (al-ibra'): Discharge or forgiveness of a debt before it is due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this lesson, which of the following is NOT a means by which the rent becomes owned?
A) Advance payment (ta'jeel)
B) Inclusion of a condition in the contract (shart)
C) The passage of time regardless of delivery
D) Actual use of the property (istifa')

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the lessor does not own the rent by the ijarah contract alone; ownership requires one of four concrete events: advance payment, a stipulation, actual use, or deliverability.

Specifying Benefit in Ijarah by Pointing
Ruling on specifying benefit in ijarah by pointing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that pointing (isharah) to the subject matter and destination specifies the benefit in ijarah and explain why this removes ambiguity (gharar).

Core Idea
Pointing to the item and destination makes the benefit known, validating the ijarah contract.

In ijarah (hiring), the benefit (manfa'ah) must be known to avoid gharar (uncertainty). The Hanafi school accepts pointing (isharah) as a valid method of specification, as this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains. Understanding this rule helps you see how practical, non-verbal actions can fulfill legal requirements in contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and its requirement
Recognize that this is an ijarah contract for transport. The key requirement is that the benefit (transport service) must be known to the parties.
2
Locate the method of specification
The text states that pointing (isharah) to the food and the destination makes the benefit known. Note that this is by consensus (ittifaqan) among Hanafi scholars.
Consensus indicates strong authority.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The reasoning is that pointing is equivalent to showing (bimanzilat al-isharah). When the hiring party shows the item and place, the benefit becomes clearly defined, removing uncertainty.
This is a form of ta'lil (legal reasoning) based on removal of gharar.
4
Derive the ruling
Because the benefit is known, the contract is valid (sahih). Pointing is thus a legally valid method of specification.
The ruling is straightforward: validity follows from knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كالاستئجار على نقل هذا الطعام إلى كذا يعني تعرف المنفعة اتفاقاً لأنه بمنزلة الإشارة لأنه إذا أراه ما ينقله والموضع الذي يحمل إليه كانت المنفعة معلومة فيصح العقد
Like hiring for transporting this food to such a place, meaning the benefit is known by agreement because it is like pointing; because when he shows him what he is transporting and the place to which it is carried, the benefit is known, so the contract is valid.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on how the benefit in an ijarah contract can be specified. The author explains that pointing (isharah) to the item to be transported and the destination suffices to make the benefit known, even if not verbally described in detail. This is by consensus (ittifaqan) among the Hanafi jurists. The reasoning is that pointing is tantamount to explicit description because it clearly identifies the subject matter and the service, thus removing ambiguity (gharar) that would invalidate the contract. This ruling is taken from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, and the commentator expands on it by noting that the benefit becomes known through this method, and the contract is valid.

Key Terms
الإشارة (al-isharah): Pointing or indicating the subject matter of the contract visually, used here to specify the benefit in ijarah.
المنفعة (al-manfa'ah): The benefit or service that is the object of the ijarah contract; here it is the transport of food.

Hire Not Owned by Contract Alone — The Four Means of Entitlement
Explanation that hire is not owned by contract alone but by one of four means

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four means by which a lessor becomes entitled to the hire in Hanafi fiqh and explain why the contract alone is insufficient.

Core Idea
The hire becomes owed gradually — entitlement arises only through payment, condition, performance, or ability to take possession.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq explains a fundamental principle of ijarah: the lessor does not own the hire merely by concluding the contract. Because the benefit is delivered over time, the countervalue is likewise owed in stages. However, the law recognizes four specific events that make the hire immediately due. Understanding this distinction is crucial for determining when the lessor can demand payment, detain the lessee, or rescind.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The hire (ujrah) is not owned by the contract alone. Why? Because the contract is a commutative exchange and the benefit is gradual, so the countervalue must also be gradual.
This is proven by the fact that if the hire were a slave relative of the lessor, immediate ownership would set him free, which does not happen.
2
State the four means of entitlement
The lessor becomes entitled to the hire only by: (1) ta'jil (prompt payment), (2) shart al-ta'jil (a condition of immediate payment), (3) istifa' (full performance of the service), or (4) tammakun (the lessee's ability to take possession).
Tammakun means handing over the premises with no hindrance; actual use is not required.
3
Examine the objection regarding ibra'
An objection might arise: if the hire is not owed, how can ibra' (remission) be valid? The author answers that ibra' is valid because it is based on the existence of the cause, like pardon for qisas after the wound.
The text notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad allows ibra' before entitlement; Abu Yusuf does not.
4
Note the ruling on sarf
If the hire is a specific commodity, sarf (money exchange) is invalid by consensus. If the hire is a debt, there is a dispute: Abu Yusuf forbids, Muhammad allows.
This affects whether the lessor can exchange the hire for other currency before receiving it.
5
Understand tammakun
Tammakun is when the premises are made available to the lessee without any hindrance. Once tammakun occurs, the lessor is entitled to the hire even if the lessee does not actually use the property.
This is a key Hanafi principle: the lessor's right is based on the opportunity to benefit, not actual use.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأجرة لا تملك بالعقد لأن العقد ينعقد شيئاً فشيئاً على حسب حدوث المنفعة على ما بينا والعقد معاوضة ومن قضيتها المساواة فمن ضرورة التراخي في جانب المنفعة التراخي في جانب البدل الآخر فلا يعتق قريب المؤجر لو كان أجرة ولا يملك المطالبة بتسليمها للحال، ولا يلزم علينا صحة الإبراء عن الأجرة والكفالة والرهن بها لأنا نقول: ذاك بناء على وجود السبب فصار كالعفو عن القصاص بعد وجود الجرح؛ كذا في غاية البيان. لكن في المحيط أن جواز الإبراء قول محمد خلافاً لأبي يوسف. وأشار المصنف إلى أنهما لو تصارفا بالأجرة فأخذ بالدراهم دنانير لا يجوز وهو قول أبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد، وإن كانت الأجرة نقرة بعينها لا تجوز المصارفة بها بالإجماع والإبراء عن بعض الأجرة صحيح الحط؛ كذا ذكره الولوالجي قوله: (بل بالتعجيل أو بشرطه أو بالاستيفاء أو بالتمكن) يعني لا يملك الأجرة إلا بواحد من هذه الأربعة والمراد أنه لا يستحقها المؤجر إلا بذلك كما أشار إليه القدوري في مختصره لأنها لو كانت ديناً لا يقال إنه ملكه المؤجر قبل قبضه، وإذا استحقها المؤجر قبل قبضها فله المطالبة بها وحبس المستأجر عليها وحبس العين عنه وله حق الفسخ إن لم يعجل له المستأجر؛ كذا في المحيط. لكن ليس له بيعها قبل قبضها. وأشار المصنف رحمه الله تعالى إلى أن المستأجر لو باع المؤجر بالأجر شيئاً وسلم جاز لتضمنه اشتراط التعجيل فتقع المقاصة بينهما، فإن تعذر إيفاء العمل رجع بالدراهم دون المتاع. والمراد من التمكن تسليم المحل إلى المستأجر بحيث لا مانع من الانتفاع
And the hire is not owned by the contract because the contract occurs gradually according to the occurrence of the benefit as we have explained, and the contract is a commutative contract, and from its requisites is equality, so from the necessity of delay on the side of the benefit is delay on the side of the other countervalue. So the relative of the lessor is not set free if he is the hire, nor does he own the right to demand delivery immediately. And it is not an objection against us the validity of remission (ibra') of the hire, and guarantee, and pledge with it, because we say: that is based on the existence of the cause, so it becomes like pardon for qisas after the wound exists. As in Ghayat al-Bayan. But in al-Muhit, the permissibility of ibra' is the saying of Muhammad contrary to Abu Yusuf. And the author indicated that if they engage in sarf with the hire, taking dirhams for dinars, it is not permissible, which is the saying of Abu Yusuf contrary to Muhammad. And if the hire is a specific piece of pure silver, sarf with it is not permissible by consensus. And remission of part of the hire is valid as a reduction (hatt); as mentioned by al-Walwaliji. His saying: 'but by prompt payment (ta'jil) or by a condition thereof, or by performance (istifa'), or by ability to take possession (tammakun)' means he does not own the hire except by one of these four. And the meaning is that the lessor does not become entitled to it except by that, as al-Quduri indicated in his Mukhtasar, because if it were a debt, it would not be said that the lessor owns it before taking possession. And if the lessor becomes entitled to it before taking possession, he has the right to demand it and to detain the lessee for it and to detain the property from him, and he has the right to rescind if the lessee does not pay promptly. As in al-Muhit. But he does not have the right to sell it before taking possession. And the author indicated that if the lessee sells to the lessor something in exchange for the hire and delivers it, it is valid because it entails a condition of prompt payment, so set-off occurs between them. If performance of the work becomes impossible, he returns to the dirhams and not the commodity. And what is meant by tammakun is handing over the premises to the lessee such that there is no hindrance to using it.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining that the hire (ujrah) is not owned by the mere contract of ijarah. The commentator argues that the contract is commutative, so since the benefit is delivered gradually, the countervalue (hire) is also owed gradually. Thus, the lessor does not become the owner of the hire immediately; otherwise, if the hire were a slave relative, he would not be set free (because immediate ownership would indicate a transfer). The correct position is that ownership/entitlement occurs via one of four means: (1) prompt payment (ta'jil) – the lessee actually pays; (2) a condition in the contract for immediate payment; (3) full performance (istifa') of the service; or (4) the lessee's ability to take possession (tammakun) of the subject matter, i.e., the premises are made available without hindrance. The commentator also addresses objections: remission (ibra') of the hire before it is owed is valid according to Muhammad but not Abu Yusuf; sarf (exchange of money) with the hire is impermissible if the hire is a specific commodity by consensus, but if it is a debt, there is disagreement. Finally, if the lessee sells something to the lessor for the hire, it is valid as a form of prompt payment. The key point is that the hire becomes a debt owed, not owned, until one of these four conditions is met.

Key Terms
التعجيل (al-ta'jil): Prompt payment of the hire by the lessee, which makes the hire owed immediately.
التمكن (al-tammakun): The lessee's ability to take possession of the hired property without hindrance, which entitles the lessor to the hire even if the lessee does not actually use it.
الإبراء (al-ibra'): Remission or release of the debt of hire by the lessor; valid according to Muhammad but not Abu Yusuf before the hire is owed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the lessor become entitled to the hire according to the text?
A) Immediately upon contract conclusion
B) Only upon full performance of the service
C) By one of four means: prompt payment, condition, performance, or ability to take possession
D) Only when the lessee actually uses the property

Key Takeaway
The lessor does not own the hire by contract alone; he becomes entitled only through ta'jil, shart al-ta'jil, istifa', or tammakun.

When Usurpation Dissolves an Ijarah Contract
Ruling on how usurpation of hired property affects the hire and the contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a hired property is usurped and explain why the hire falls proportionally, including the dispute with Qadikhan.

Core Idea
Prevention of the lessee from using the property dissolves the contract and drops the hire proportionally.

Usurpation (ghasb) in ijarah is not about physical seizure—it is about barring the lessee from benefit. This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq explains that if the lessee is prevented from using the hired property, the hire falls because delivery of the premises stands for delivery of the benefit. The author clarifies that this applies even to real estate (where technical ghasb does not apply) and covers partial prevention. Dispute resolution rules based on current possession are also provided.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and its rationale
Find the principle: since delivering the premises enables benefit, prevention nullifies delivery and drops the hire. Note the ‘illa (legal cause).
2
Note the ikhtilāf with Qāḍīkhān
The text states that the contract dissolves according to al-Hidāyah, contrary to Qāḍīkhān. Understand both positions.
3
Apply to full and partial prevention
If the entire term is prevented, all hire falls; if part, it falls proportionally. This includes the ‘one room’ example.
4
Understand the dispute resolution rules
When there is no evidence, the current state of possession determines who bears the burden. Example: the mill and water flow case.
5
Recognize the practical scope
The ruling covers real estate and movables, and prevention can come from the lessor, a third party, or even the first occupant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن غصب منه سقط الأجر لأن تسليم المحل إنما أقيم مقام تسليم المنفعة للتمكن من الانتفاع فإذا فات التمكن فات التسليم. وأشار بقوله سقط الأجر إلى أن العقد ينفسخ بالغصب كما صرح به في الهداية خلافاً لقاضيخان. وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا غصب في جميع المدة فيسقط جميع الأجر وما إذا غصب في بعضها فبحسابه، وشمل العقار وغيره ومراده من الغصب هنا الحيلولة بين المستأجر والعين لا حقيقته إذ الغصب لا يجري في العقار عندنا، وشمل ما إذا حال بينه وبين الساكن الأوّل، فلو ادعى ذلك المستأجر وأنكره المؤجر ولا بينة يحكم الحال فإن كان المستأجر هو الساكن في الدار حال المنازعة فالقول للمؤجر، وإن كان فيها غير المستأجر فالقول للمستأجر ولا أجر عليه كمسألة الطاحونة وهي لو وقع الاختلاف بين مستأجر الطاحونة والأجر بعد انقضاء المدة في جريان الماء وانقطاعه فإنه يحكم الحال، فإن كان جارياً حال المنازعة فالقول قول من يدعي دوام التسليم وإلا فالقول لمدعي زواله ولا يقبل قول الساكن في المسألة الأولى على غيره لأنه فرد؛ كذا في الذخيرة. وشمل ما إذا حال بينه وبين العين المؤجر أيضاً وكذا لو سلمه إلا بيتاً فإنه يسقط عنه بحسابه؛ كذا في المحيط. وكذا لو سكن معه في الدار؛ كذا في الخلاصة.
If it is usurped from him, the hire falls because handing over the premises is only established in place of handing over the benefit for the ability to use. So when the ability is lost, the handing over is lost. And by his saying 'the hire falls' he indicates that the contract is dissolved by usurpation, as stated in al-Hidayah, contrary to Qadikhan. And he made it absolute, so it includes if the usurpation is for the entire duration, then all the hire falls, and if in part, then proportionally. And it includes real estate and other things. And by usurpation here he means preventing the lessee from accessing the property, not its literal meaning, since usurpation does not apply to real estate in our school. And it includes if he prevents the first occupant. So if the lessee claims that and the lessor denies it and there is no evidence, the present situation is judged: if the lessee is the occupant of the house at the time of dispute, the say is the lessor's; if there is someone else in it, the say is the lessee's and no hire is due on him, like the mill case: if a dispute occurs between the mill lessee and the lessor after the term regarding the water flow and its interruption, the present situation is judged. If the water is flowing at the time of dispute, the say is of the one who claims continuity of delivery; otherwise the say is of the one who claims its cessation. And the statement of the occupant in the first case is not accepted against others because he is a party. As in al-Dhakhira. And it includes if he prevents him from the hired property itself, and also if he handed over except a room, then it falls proportionally; as in al-Muhit. And also if he lives with him in the house; as in al-Khulasa.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the effect of ghasb (usurpation) on an ijarah contract. The principle is that delivering the premises is equivalent to delivering the benefit because it enables the lessee to use. If the lessee is prevented from using (by usurpation from the lessor or a third party), the delivery is considered null, and the hire falls. The commentator clarifies that 'sakat al-ajr' indicates the contract is dissolved (yansakh) according to al-Hidayah, contrary to Qadikhan's view that the contract remains. The ruling is general: if the entire period is usurped, all hire falls; if part, proportionally. It applies to both movable and immovable property, but 'ghasb' here means prevention, not the technical tort, since in Hanafi law, ghasb as a tort does not apply to real estate. The passage also provides rules for disputes between lessor and lessee: the current possession is presumed valid unless evidence is provided. For example, in a mill dispute, if the water is flowing at the time of dispute, the presumption is in favor of delivery. Partial prevention (e.g., one room not handed over) leads to proportional reduction of hire. The relied-upon view is that the contract dissolves.

Key Terms
الغصب (al-ghasb): Prevention of the lessee from accessing the hired property, not the technical tort of usurpation since that does not apply to real estate in Hanafi law.
الحيلولة (al-hayulah): Interposition or prevention; the act of barring the lessee from using the property.
ينفسخ (yansakh): The contract is dissolved; it terminates due to the prevention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (mufta bihi), what happens to the ijarah contract if the lessor prevents the lessee from using the property for part of the rental term?
A) The contract becomes void from the beginning (batil)
B) The contract remains valid and the hire is due in full
C) The contract dissolves and the hire drops proportionally for the period of prevention
D) The contract is suspended and resumes after prevention ends

Key Takeaway
Prevention of the lessee from using the hired property, whether full or partial, by any party, dissolves the ijarah contract and drops the hire proportionally.

When Hire Becomes Due for Houses, Camel Drivers, and Craftsmen
Rulings on when the lessor can demand hire for houses, camel drivers, and craftsmen

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on when hire is due for continuous benefit, transport by stage, and piecework crafts, and identify the relied-upon position in the building dispute.

Core Idea
Hire for continuous benefit is due daily; for transport per stage; for piecework only after completion.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rules on when a lessor can demand hire. The passage distinguishes between types of work: continuous benefits like housing, sequential services like camel driving, and piecework like tailoring. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly applying ijarah contracts in practice. The passage also addresses a dispute on building contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The passage divides hire entitlement into three categories: continuous benefit (house/land), transport (camel driver), and crafts (tailor/washer). For each, note the time of entitlement.
2
Analyze the rationale for each
For houses, the benefit is divisible by day; for camel drivers, each stage is a distinct desired benefit; for craftsmen, partial work is not independently beneficial, so hire is due only after completion and delivery.
3
Note contractual specification
If the contract specifies a payment time, that overrides the default as it is considered a condition of prompt payment.
4
Examine the building contract dispute
The passage notes a difference of opinion: al-Hidayah denies hire for partial building work, but the relied-upon madhhab (from al-Asl and al-Karkhi) allows it if the part is handed over.
5
Apply to modern scenarios
These rulings apply to modern rentals (daily vs monthly) and services paid per milestone or per unit of work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولرب الدار والأرض طلب الأجر كل يوم لأنه منفعة مقصودة وما دون اليوم لا حد له فصار كالنفقة لها طلبها عند المساء في كل ساعة أراد به ما إذا أطلقه، أما إذا بين وقت الاستحقاق في العقد تعين لأنه بمنزلة التعجيل كما إذا قال أجرتك هذه الدار سنة على أن تعطي الأجرة بعد شهرين قوله: (وللجمال كل مرحلة) لأن سير كل مرحلة مقصود قوله: (وللقصار والخياط بعد الفراغ من عمله) لأن العمل في البعض غير منتفع به فلا يستوجب به الأجر، وأراد به ما إذا سلمه فأفاد أنه لو هلك في يده قبل التسليم فلا أجر له، وكذا كل من لعمله أثر وإن لم يكن لعمله أثر فكما فرغ منه استحق الأجر، وإن لم يسلمها كالجمال والملاح فلا يسقط الأجر في الهلاك بعده وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الخياط في بيت المستأجر فإنه لا يستحق ببعض العمل شيئاً لما قدمناه واختاره في الهداية. ويتفرع عليه أيضاً ما إذا استأجره لبناء داره فبنى البعض ثم انهدم فلا أجر له، ولا يستحق الأجر على البعض إلا في سكنى الدار وقطع المسافة، واختار جماعة من مشايخنا خلافه. ومسألة البناء منصوص عليها في الأصل أنه يجب الأجر بالبعض لكونه مسلماً إلى المستأجر، ونقله الكرخي عن أصحابنا وجزم به في غاية البيان رداً على الهداية فكان هو المذهب ولهذا اختاره المصنف في المستصفى وإن كانت عبارته هنا مطلقة
And for the owner of the house and land, demanding the hire every day because it is a desired benefit, and what is less than a day has no limit, so it is like maintenance, which can be demanded at evening every hour. He meant when it is absolute. But if the time of entitlement is specified in the contract, it is fixed, because it is like a condition of prompt payment, as if he says: I hire this house to you for a year on condition that you give the hire after two months. His saying: (And for the camel driver every stage) because traveling each stage is a desired purpose. His saying: (And for the washer and tailor after finishing his work) because the work in part is not benefited from, so he does not become entitled to hire for it. And he meant when he hands it over; thus if it perishes in his hand before delivery, no hire for him. And likewise everyone whose work has an effect, and if his work has no effect, then as soon as he finishes he becomes entitled to hire, even if he does not hand it over, like the camel driver and the sailor, the hire does not fall if it perishes afterwards. And he made it absolute, so it includes if the tailor is in the lessee's house, then he is not entitled to anything for part of the work as we have presented, and that is chosen in al-Hidayah. And it also branches out: if he hires him to build his house and he builds part then it collapses, no hire for him. And he is not entitled to hire for part except in the dwelling of the house and covering the distance. And a group of our masters chose the opposite. And the case of building is stated in al-Asl that hire is due for the part because it is handed over to the lessee, and al-Karkhi transmitted it from our companions and affirmed it in Ghayat al-Bayan, rejecting al-Hidayah, so that is the madhhab, and for this reason the author chose it in al-Mustasfa, even though his expression here is absolute.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage details when the hire becomes due for different types of ijarah contracts. For houses and land, the benefit is continuous and divisible by day, so the lessor can demand hire daily because a shorter period has no fixed limit. However, if the contract specifies a payment time, that governs. For camel drivers, hire is due per stage (marhala) because each leg of the journey is a distinct desired benefit. For craftsmen like tailors and washers, hire is due only after completion of the entire work, because partial work is not independently beneficial; the product must be delivered. If the item perishes before delivery, no hire is due. But for workers like camel drivers or sailors whose service is continuous, hire is earned as the work progresses, and if the item perishes after the work, the hire remains due. The passage also notes a dispute: for building contracts, the relied-upon view (from al-Asl and al-Karkhi) is that hire is due for completed parts handed over, contrary to what is stated in al-Hidayah. The author's expression here seems absolute, but the chosen madhhab is that hire is due for partial building work. This ruling applies to cases where a house is hired: the lessor can demand daily hire unless otherwise agreed.

Key Terms
المرحلة (al-marhalah): A stage or leg of a journey; the unit for which a camel driver is entitled to hire.
الاستيفاء (al-istifa'): Full performance or completion of the work; for craftsmen, hire is due only after istifa' and delivery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when can the owner of a hired house demand the rent?
A) Only after the full term ends
B) At the end of each day
C) At the end of each month
D) At any time as he wishes

Key Takeaway
Hire is due daily for continuous benefits, per stage for transport, and after completion for piecework; for building contracts, the relied-upon view entitles hire for completed parts handed over.

Effect of Ghasb on Lease Contracts: Annulment and Wage Drop
Intra-Hanafi dispute over contract annulment due to usurpation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of ghasb on an ijarah contract and explain the disagreement between Al-Hidayah and Qadi Khan.

Core Idea
Prevention of access annuls the lease contract and drops the wage proportionally.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a critical issue in Islamic lease law: what happens when the lessee is prevented from using the property? The ruling hinges on a principle that delivery of the place is equivalent to delivery of the benefit. We'll examine the ruling, its rationale, and the internal Hanafi dispute between the position in Al-Hidayah and Qadi Khan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is ghasb (prevention of access) occurring during an ijarah contract. The ruling stated is that the wage drops. Determine whether this applies to full or partial prevention.
The text uses 'ghasb' in a broad sense, not the technical legal definition.
2
Understand the rationale (talil)
The commentator explains that delivery of the place (the leased property) is made equivalent to delivery of the benefit (usufruct). If the lessee cannot access the property, delivery of the benefit is lost, so the wage obligation falls.
This is a qiyas: the place stands in for the benefit in terms of delivery.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Al-Hidayah holds that the contract is annulled by ghasb. Qadi Khan disagrees, holding that the contract remains valid but the wage drops. Identify the mufta bihi position.
The difference has practical implications: if annulled, the contract ends; if not, it revives when access is restored.
4
Apply the rule to partial prevention
The text states that if prevention occurs for part of the period, the wage drops proportionally. This applies whether the property is real estate or movable, and includes cases where the lessor himself prevents access.
Example: if one room is withheld, the wage for that room is deducted proportionally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن غصب منه سقط الأجر) لأن تسليم المحل إنما أقيم مقام تسليم المنفعة للتمكن من الانتفاع فإذا فات التمكن فات التسليم. وأشار بقوله سقط الأجر» إلى أن العقد ينفسخ بالغصب كما صرح به في الهداية خلافاً لقاضيخان . وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا غصب في جميع المدة فيسقط جميع الأجر وما إذا غصب في بعضها فبحسابه، وشمل العقار وغيره ومراده من الغصب هنا الحيلولة بين المستأجر والعين لا حقيقته إذ الغصب لا يجري في العقار عندنا، وشمل ما إذا حال بينه وبين الساكن الأوّل، فلو ادعى ذلك المستأجر وأنكره المؤجر ولا بينة يحكم الحال فإن كان المستأجر هو الساكن في الدار حال المنازعة فالقول للمؤجر، وإن كان فيها غير المستأجر فالقول للمستأجر ولا أجر عليه كمسألة الطاحونة وهي لو وقع الاختلاف بين مستأجر الطاحونة والأجر بعد انقضاء المدة في جريان الماء وانقطاعه فإنه يحكم الحال، فإن كان جارياً حال المنازعة فالقول قول من يدعي دوام التسليم وإلا فالقول لمدعي زواله ولا يقبل قول الساكن في المسألة الأولى على غيره لأنه فرد ؛ كذا في الذخيرة. وشمل ما إذا حال بينه وبين العين المؤجر أيضاً وكذا لو سلمه إلا بيتاً فإنه يسقط عنه بحسابه ؛ كذا في المحيط . وكذا لو سكن معه . في الدار؛ كذا في الخلاصة .
He said: (If [the property] is usurped from him, the wage drops) because delivery of the place is made equivalent to delivery of the benefit for the ability to use, so when ability is lost, delivery is lost. And by saying 'the wage drops' he indicated that the contract is annulled by usurpation, as stated in Al-Hidayah, contrary to Qadi Khan. And he gave it generally, including if usurped for the whole period then all wage drops, and if for part then proportionally. It includes real estate and other, and his intent by usurpation here is prevention of access between lessee and property, not its reality, since usurpation does not apply to real estate in our [school]. It includes if [the lessor] prevents between him and the first occupant. If the lessee claims that and the lessor denies without evidence, judgment is based on the present situation: if the lessee is the occupant at the time of dispute, the word is with the lessor; if a non-lessee is in the property, the word is with the lessee and no wage due, like the mill case. [The text] includes if he prevents from the leased property itself, and also if he delivered except one room, then proportionally drops. Similarly if he lives with him in the house.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage addresses the effect of ghasb (usurpation) on an ijarah (lease) contract. The ruling is that if the lessee is prevented from using the leased property, the wage obligation falls. The commentator clarifies that this applies whether the prevention is for the whole period or part of it. The term 'ghasb' here is used in a broad sense—meaning prevention of access—not the technical legal definition, because in the Hanafi school, ghasb in its strict sense does not apply to immovable property (since land cannot be physically seized). The contract is annulled by such prevention, as stated in Al-Hidayah, though Qadi Khan differed. The passage also provides rules for disputes: if the lessee claims prevention and the lessor denies, the judgment depends on who is currently in possession. If the lessee is in possession, the lessor's word is taken; if another person is in possession, the lessee's word is taken and no wage is due. This is illustrated with the example of a mill where water flow may be interrupted. The ruling extends to partial prevention, such as the lessor delivering the property except one room, in which case the wage is reduced proportionally.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Prevention of access to the leased property, not the legal definition of usurpation (taking property by force).
حيلولة (haylulah): Prevention or obstruction between the lessee and the property.
انفساخ (infisakh): Annulment of the contract due to an external cause, such as ghasb, without requiring a court order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to an ijarah contract if the lessee is prevented from using the property for the entire lease period?
A) The contract remains valid but the wage is void.
B) The contract is annulled and the wage is void.
C) The contract is void from the beginning.
D) The lessor must refund the wage and the contract continues.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, prevention of access (ghasb) annuls the lease contract, causing the wage to drop proportionally for the period of prevention.

Resolving Disputes Over Usurpation in Lease: The Role of Possession
Procedural rule for burden of proof in ghasb disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for determining who bears the burden of proof when a lessee claims ghasb and the lessor denies.

Core Idea
In disputes over prevention, judgment follows current possession: the occupant's word prevails.

This passage also provides a procedural rule for resolving disputes when the lessee claims he was prevented from using the property but the lessor denies it. The judge looks at who is currently in possession. This rule ensures justice without requiring witnesses. We'll examine the rule, its application to different scenarios, and the famous 'mill case' example.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
The lessee claims ghasb (prevention), the lessor denies, and neither has witnesses. How does the judge decide?
The dispute is about whether prevention occurred during the lease period.
2
Apply the rule based on current possession
If the lessee is currently occupying the property, the lessor's word is taken (i.e., the lessor's denial is believed). If another person (not the lessee) is in possession, the lessee's word is taken, and no wage is due.
This is because possession is a strong indicator of continuous access.
3
Understand the rationale
The rule relies on the apparent state (hal). If the lessee is in possession, it suggests he can use the property, so the lessor's denial of prevention is stronger. If someone else is there, it suggests the lessee was excluded, supporting his claim.
The 'mill case' (taahunah) is a similar example: if water is flowing, the person claiming continuous delivery is believed; if not, the person claiming stoppage is believed.
4
Apply to partial prevention and other variations
The rule also applies if the lessor prevented access completely, or delivered except one room, or even moved in himself. In each case, the wage adjustment follows the same principle.
The text mentions 'if he lives with him' implying that cohabitation by the lessor is a form of prevention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

He said: (If [the property] is usurped from him, the wage drops) because delivery of the place is made equivalent to delivery of the benefit for the ability to use, so when ability is lost, delivery is lost. And by saying 'the wage drops' he indicated that the contract is annulled by usurpation, as stated in Al-Hidayah, contrary to Qadi Khan. And he gave it generally, including if usurped for the whole period then all wage drops, and if for part then proportionally. Commentary
This passage addresses the effect of ghasb (usurpation) on an ijarah (lease) contract. The ruling is that if the lessee is prevented from using the leased property, the wage obligation falls. The commentator clarifies that this applies whether the prevention is for the whole period or part of it. The term 'ghasb' here is used in a broad sense—meaning prevention of access—not the technical legal definition, because in the Hanafi school, ghasb in its strict sense does not apply to immovable property (since land cannot be physically seized). The contract is annulled by such prevention, as stated in Al-Hidayah, though Qadi Khan differed. The passage also provides rules for disputes: if the lessee claims prevention and the lessor denies, the judgment depends on who is currently in possession. If the lessee is in possession, the lessor's word is taken; if another person is in possession, the lessee's word is taken and no wage is due. This is illustrated with the example of a mill where water flow may be interrupted. The ruling extends to partial prevention, such as the lessor delivering the property except one room, in which case the wage is reduced proportionally.

Key Terms
حال (hal): The current state or situation, used as evidence in disputes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute over ghasb without witnesses, who is believed if the lessee is currently living in the property?
A) The lessee is believed.
B) The lessor is believed.
C) The judge asks for witnesses despite their absence.
D) Both are believed equally, and the wage is split.

Key Takeaway
In disputes over prevention without evidence, the current state of possession determines whose word is taken: the lessor's if the lessee is in possession, the lessee's if another occupies the property.

Timing of Wage in Ijara: Daily for House, Per Stage for Camel
Ruling on timing of wage for house/land and camel hire

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default timing of wage demand for house/land and camel hire, and explain the reasoning (talil) based on the nature of the benefit.

Core Idea
Wage for house/land is due daily, for camel per stage, because each unit of benefit is consumable and measurable.

In many lease contracts, the timing of wage payment can be ambiguous. The Hanafi school provides clear default rules based on the nature of the benefit. For houses and land, the benefit is consumed day by day, so the lessor can demand wage daily. For camel drivers, the benefit is measured by stages of travel. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind these rulings and explains when specification in the contract overrides the default.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two lease types
The passage covers two distinct scenarios: (1) lease of a house or land, and (2) hire of a camel (or driver) for transport. Note the different units of benefit.
House/land: benefit per day. Camel: benefit per stage (marhalah).
2
State the default ruling for each
For an absolute contract (no specified payment time), the lessor of house/land may demand the wage every day. For the camel driver, wage is due after each stage.
Default applies when contract is absolute.
3
Understand the reasoning (talil)
The ruling is based on the concept of 'manfa'ah maqsudah' (desired benefit). For house/land, less than a day cannot be a meaningful unit, so daily wage is like maintenance (nafaqah) which is due daily. For camel, each stage is a distinct desired benefit.
Analogy to nafaqah (maintenance) for house.
4
Recognize the exception
If the contract specifies a payment time, that specification is binding. It is treated like advance payment (ta'jil).
Example: 'I lease this house for a year on condition that you pay after two months.'
5
Apply the ruling
Given a new scenario (e.g., lease of a shop, hire of a truck driver), determine the default timing of wage based on the nature of the benefit.
Consider whether the benefit is consumed continuously or in stages.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولرب الدار والأرض طلب الأجر كل يوم لأنه منفعة مقصودة وما دون اليوم لا حد له فصار كالنفقة لها طلبها عند المساء في كل ساعة أراد به ما إذا أطلقه، أما إذا بين وقت الاستحقاق في العقد تعين لأنه بمنزلة التعجيل كما إذا قال أجرتك هذه الدار سنة على أن تعطي الأجرة بعد شهرين قوله : ( وللجمال كل مرحلة لأن سير كل مرحلة مقصود
He said: (And for the owner of the house and land, demanding the wage every day) because it is a desired benefit, and less than a day has no limit, so it becomes like maintenance, for which she asks at evening every hour. He intended this when [the time] is absolute; if the time of entitlement is specified in the contract, it becomes fixed because it is like advance payment, as if he said 'I lease this house to you for a year on condition that you give the wage after two months.' He said: (And for the camel driver, every stage) because the travel of each stage is desired.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage explains the timing of wage entitlement for different types of hire contracts. For the lease of a house or land, the lessor may demand the wage every day because the benefit (use) is consumed daily. Since less than a day cannot be a meaningful unit, the wage is like maintenance (nafaqah) which is due daily. However, if the contract specifies a time for payment, that specification is binding. For a camel driver hired for transport, the wage becomes due after each stage (a measure of distance) because each stage is a distinct desired benefit. The commentator notes that the ruling applies when the contract is absolute; if payment time is specified, it governs.

Key Terms
منفعة مقصودة (manfa'ah maqsudah): A benefit that is intended and has a measurable unit (e.g., daily use).
مرحلة (marhalah): A stage or measure of distance in travel, used as a unit for camel hire.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a lease of a house without specifying payment time, when can the lessor demand the wage?
A) Only at the end of the lease term.
B) Daily, because each day is a distinct benefit.
C) Monthly, following general custom.
D) At any time, as per the lessor's discretion.

Key Takeaway
In an absolute ijara contract, wage for house/land is due daily and for camel hire per stage, reflecting the unit of benefit consumed.
