Timing of Wage for Tailor and Launderer
Ruling with proof on wage timing, with expansions and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wage entitlement for tailors and launderers, explain the exception for workers without tangible effect, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi disputes on partial building work and unnamed fees.

Core Idea
Wage for a tailor is due only after completion and delivery; but a camel driver gets paid upon finishing, even if the goods perish later.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a key principle in hire contracts: wage entitlement depends on delivery of the completed benefit. The text distinguishes between workers whose work leaves a tangible effect and those whose benefit is consumed instantly. It also addresses two contested cases—the partial building collapse and the launderer working without a named fee—that have practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and its rationale
The matn states that the launderer and tailor are entitled to wage only after completion of work and delivery. The reason (ʿilla) is that partial work is not beneficial. This applies when the item is delivered to the customer; if it perishes before delivery, no wage is due.
This is the default rule for workers whose work leaves a tangible effect (e.g., sewing, washing).
2
Distinguish workers with and without tangible effect
Workers like camel drivers and sailors have no tangible effect; their benefit is immediate consumption of transport. For them, wage is due as soon as they finish the service, even if they never deliver the goods physically. Later destruction does not cancel the wage.
The distinction is based on whether the work produces a visible, durable result.
3
Analyze the building collapse dispute
If a builder is hired to build a house and part collapses before full completion, Al-Hidayah says no wage for the part because it is not beneficial alone. However, the original sources (nass) and scholars like al-Karkhi and al-Mustasfa rule that wage is due for the delivered part because it was physically handed over to the owner. This is the mufta bihi.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi; the majority supports wage for partial delivery.
4
Examine the launderer fee dispute
If a launderer is given cloth to wash without naming a fee, Abu Hanifa says no wage at all. Muhammad says if the launderer is known to accept such work for hire (by custom), he is entitled to the customary wage. The fatwa follows Muhammad's view.
This shows the role of ʿurf (custom) in determining wage entitlement.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and authority weight
For the building case, the majority view (wage for partial delivery) is mufta bihi, supported by al-Karkhi and the author in al-Mustasfa. For the launderer, the fatwa is on Muhammad's saying. These rulings come from zahir al-riwayah and later preferred positions.
The hierarchy: explicit nass in the sources overrides the opinion in Al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وللقصار والخياط بعد الفراغ من عمله لأن العمل في البعض غير منتفع به فلا يستوجب به الأجر، وأراد به ما إذا سلمه فأفاد أنه لو هلك في يده قبل التسليم فلا أجر له، وكذا كل من . لعمله أثر وإن لم يكن لعمله أثر فكما فرغ منه استحق الأجر، وإن لم يسلمها كالجمال والملاح فلا يسقط الأجر في الهلاك بعده وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الخياط في بيت المستأجر فإنه لا يستحق ببعض العمل شيئاً لما قدمناه واختاره في الهداية. ويتفرع عليه أيضاً ما إذا استأجره لبناء داره فبنى البعض ثم انهدم فلا أجر له، ولا يستحق الأجر على البعض إلا في سكنى الدار وقطع المسافة، واختار جماعة من مشايخنا خلافه. ومسألة البناء منصوص عليها في الأصل أنه يجب الأجر بالبعض لكونه مسلماً إلى المستأجر، ونقله الكرخي عن أصحابنا وجزم به في غاية البيان رداً على الهداية فكان هو المذهب ولهذا اختاره المصنف في المستصفى وإن كانت عبارته هنا مطلقة وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية الخيط والمخيط على الخياط أنه وللخباز بعد إخراج الخبز من التنور فإن أخرجه فاحترق له الأجر ولا ضمان عليه وهذا في عرفهم، أما في عرفنا فالخيط على صاحب الثوب، وفي المخيط الخياط إذا خاطه بأجر ففتقه رجل قبل أن يقبضه رب الثوب فلا أجر للخياط ولا يجبر على الإعادة، وإن كان الخياط هو الذي فتقه فعليه الإعادة كأنه لم يعمل بخلاف ما إذا فتقه الأجنبي ألا يلزمه الضمان وفي الخياط لا يلزمه اهـ. ولا يخفى أن ما ضمنه الأجنبي يكون للخياط لكونه بدل ما أتلفه عليه حتى سقطت أجرته. وفي الخلاصة رجل دفع إلى خياط ثوباً ليخيطه فقطعه ومات لا يجب شيء من الأجرة لأن الأجر في العادة للخياطة لا للقطع وهو الأصح اهـ. وفي الفتاوى الصغرى : إذا دفع ثوباً لقصار ليقصره ولم يسم له أجراً قال أبو حنيفة : لا أجر له. وقال محمد: إن انتصب القصار لقبول ذلك من الناس بالأجر كما وإلا فلا. قال في الخلاصة معزياً إلى الصدر الشهيد والفتوى على قول محمد
He said: (And for the launderer and tailor, after completion of his work) because work on part is not beneficial, so it does not necessitate wage. He intended that when he delivers it, so it indicates that if it perishes in his hand before delivery, no wage; similarly anyone whose work has an effect, even if no effect, as soon as he finishes he becomes entitled, even if he has not delivered, like the camel driver and sailor, the wage does not drop due to later destruction. He gave it generally, including if the tailor works in the lessee's house, then he is not entitled to wage for partial work. It also branches to if he hired him to build a house and he built part then it collapsed, no wage; and he is not entitled for part except in dwelling and travel. A group of our scholars chose contrary. The building case is explicitly stated in the source that wage is due for partial work because it was delivered to the lessee, and al-Karkhi transmitted from our companions and affirmed it in Ghayat al-Bayan in refutation of Al-Hidayah, so that is the school, and for this the author chose it in al-Mustasfa. In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: the thread and sewing are on the tailor; that and for baker after removing bread from oven; if he removed it and it burned, he gets wage and no liability, and this is in their custom; but in our custom the thread is on the owner of the cloth. If a tailor sews for hire and a man tears it before the owner receives it, no wage for tailor and he is not forced to redo; if the tailor himself tore it, he must redo as if he did nothing, unlike if a stranger tore it, he must guarantee? In the tailor, he does not? It is not hidden that what the stranger guarantees becomes for the tailor as compensation for what he destroyed, so his wage drops. In al-Khulasa: a man gave cloth to a tailor to sew, he cut it and died, no wage is due because customarily wage is for sewing not cutting, and that is the most correct. In al-Fatawa al-Sughra: if one gives cloth to a launderer to launder without naming a wage, Abu Hanifa said: no wage for him. Muhammad said: if the launderer is established to accept such work for wage, then he gets wage; otherwise not. In al-Khulasa citing al-Sadr al-Shahid, the fatwa is on Muhammad's saying.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage discusses wage entitlement for tailors and launderers whose work is piecework. Entitlement to wage occurs only after completion of the entire work and delivery (or equivalent), because partial work does not yet benefit the customer. If the item perishes before delivery, no wage is due. However, for workers whose work does not leave a tangible effect (like a camel driver or sailor), wage is due upon completion even before delivery because the benefit is consumed immediately. The passage also addresses a disputed case: if a tailor builds part of a house and it collapses, some scholars (including the author in al-Mustasfa) say wage is due for the part because it was delivered to the occupier, while Al-Hidayah says no wage. The more accepted view is that wage is due for partial delivery. Additionally, the text covers: matter of thread in tailoring (in some customs, thread is on tailor, in others on owner), consequences if a third party tears the garment (if stranger tore, he compensates tailor who then loses wage; if tailor tore, he must redo without extra pay), and the case of a launderer who cuts and dies (no wage because wage is for laundering, not cutting). Finally, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute about a launderer who works without naming a wage: Abu Hanifa says no wage, Muhammad says if he is known to work for hire, he gets payment by custom. The fatwa follows Muhammad.

Key Terms
قصار (qassar): Launderer or one who cleans clothes by stamping/washing.
خياط (khayyat): Tailor who sews cloth.
الخيط والمخيط (al-khayt wa al-mikhyat): The thread (materials) and the sewing (labor); a phrase determining responsibility for supplies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (operative) view of the Hanafi school, if a builder is hired to build a house and completes part that collapses before the house is finished, is he entitled to any wage?
A) No wage, because the whole house was not completed.
B) Yes, wage for the part that was delivered to the owner.
C) Yes, but only if the collapse was not his fault.
D) No wage, because partial building is not beneficial.

Key Takeaway
For workers with tangible effect, wage is due only after completion and delivery; for those without, wage upon completion; and intra-Hanafi disputes often center on the definition of benefit (manfaʿa).

Baker's Wage After Removal and Liability for Burning
Intra-Hanafi dispute on baker's liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi positions on a baker's wage entitlement and liability when bread burns or is stolen after removal from the oven, and apply the mufta bihi ruling in a given scenario.

Core Idea
Baker's wage depends on delivery; liability for loss after removal splits Abu Hanifa from the Sahibayn.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a practical dispute: when a hired baker removes bread from the oven but it burns or is stolen before delivery. The ruling hinges on where the baking occurred and whose custody the bread is in. Understanding this intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf clarifies the distinction between an amanah and a common hireling's liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and default ruling
First, note the two main scenarios: baking in the customer's house vs. baking in the baker's own shop. The default rule is that wage is due upon removal if the bread is in the customer's house (delivery by placement).
2
Locate the ikhtilaf
The dispute arises when baking occurs in the baker's own shop and the bread is stolen or burns after removal but before delivery. Abu Hanifa holds no liability (amanah), while the Sahibayn hold the baker responsible as a common hireling.
3
Understand each position's proof
Abu Hanifa: the bread is an amanah (trust) in the baker's possession; no transgression, so no liability, and wage is not due because delivery hasn't occurred. The Sahibayn: the baker is an ajir mushtarak (common hireling) and is liable for the work product; the customer has an option between flour compensation (no wage) or bread value (with wage).
4
Analyze the conditions
The text conditions the ruling on when the burning occurs. If before removal (in the oven), the baker is liable due to negligence (consensus). If after removal, the location determines the ruling.
5
Apply the thamarah (practical consequence)
Under Abu Hanifa: baker loses wage but no compensation. Under Sahibayn: customer can choose flour or bread compensation with corresponding wage adjustment. The mufta bihi in later practice is often the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللخباز بعد إخراج الخبز من التنور لأن تمام العمل بالإخراج أطلقه فأفاد أنه يستحق بإخراج البعض بقدره لأن العمل في ذلك القدر صار مسلماً إلى صاحب الدقيق؛ كذا في غاية البيان والجوهرة. ومراده إذا كان الخبز في بيت المستأجر لأنه صار مسلماً إليه بمجرد الإخراج كما صرح به في مستصفاه ، أما إذا كان خارجاً عن بيت المستأجر سواء كان في بيت الخباز أو لا فلا يستحق الأجرة إلا بالتسليم حقيقة وفي الجوهرة: فإن سرق الخبز بعدما أخرجه فإن كان يخبز في بيت صاحب الطعام فله الأجرة، وإن كان يخبز في بيت الخباز فلا أجرة له لعدم التسليم ولا ضمان عليه فيما سرق عند أبي حنيفة لأنه أمانة خلافاً لهما الأجير المشترك . في يده هو المعتاد يجب وهي مسألة قوله : (فإن أخرجه فاحترق فله الأجر ولا ضمان عليه لأنه صار مسلماً بالوضع في بيته فاستحق المسمى ولم يوجد منه جناية فلا ضمان عليه إجماعاً فأفاد أنه لو كان الخبز في غير بيت المستأجر فاحترق فلا أجر له ولا ضمان عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما إن شاء ضمنه دقيقاً مثل دقيقه ولا أجر له وإن شاء ضمنه قيمة الخبز وأعطاه الأجر ولا يجب عليه ضمان الحطب والملح. وقيد بكونه احترق عقيب الإخراج لأنه إذا احترق قبل الإخراج فعليه الضمان في قول أصحابنا جميعاً لأنه مما جنته يداه بتقصيره في القلع من التنور فإن ضمنه قيمته مخبوزاً أعطاه الأجر، وإن ضمنه دقيقاً لم يكن له أجر ؛ كذا في غاية البيان
And for the baker, after removing the bread from the oven, because completion of work is by removal. He gave it generally, so it indicates that he is entitled for removal of part proportionally, because the work in that amount becomes delivered to the owner of the flour. This is in Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Jawharah. And his intent is when the bread is in the lessee's house, because it becomes delivered to him by mere removal, as stated in his Mustasfa. But if it is outside the lessee's house, whether in the baker's house or not, he is not entitled to the wage except by actual delivery. In al-Jawharah: If the bread is stolen after he removed it, if he baked in the food-owner's house, he gets the wage; if he baked in the baker's house, no wage due to lack of delivery, and no liability for what was stolen according to Abu Hanifa because it is an amanah (trust), contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the common hireling? In his hand, the custom necessitates? And this is the issue. He said: (If he removed it and it burned, he gets the wage and no liability) because it became delivered by placing in his house, so he is entitled to the named wage, and no transgression existed from him, so no liability by consensus. So it indicates that if the bread was in a place other than the lessee's house and burned, then no wage and no liability according to Abu Hanifa, while according to the two (disciples), if he wishes he guarantees flour like his flour and no wage, and if he wishes he guarantees the value of bread and gives the wage, and he is not liable for firewood and salt. And it is conditioned that it burn immediately after removal because if it burns before removal, he is liable according to all our scholars because it is caused by his own hands due to negligence in removing from the oven. If he guarantees its value as baked, he gives him the wage; if he guarantees flour, no wage. This is in Ghayat al-Bayan.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage explains the baker's entitlement to wage and liability issues. According to the text, a baker is entitled to his wage after removing the bread from the oven, because the work is completed by removal. If he bakes in the customer's house, removal constitutes delivery, so wage is due immediately, even if the bread is later stolen or burned. If he bakes in his own shop, wage is due only upon actual delivery (handing over). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute (Abu Hanifa vs. the two disciples) regarding liability if the bread is stolen or burns after removal but before delivery. Abu Hanifa holds that the baker is not liable because the bread is in his possession as an amanah (trust) until delivery. The disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) give the customer an option: either claim flour-like compensation with no wage, or claim value of bread with wage. For burning immediately after removal in the baker's own place, Abu Hanifa says no wage and no liability; the disciples give option. If the bread burns before removal (e.g., in the oven), the baker is liable by all because of negligence, and the compensation affects wage entitlement.

Key Terms
خباز (khabbaz): Baker who bakes bread for hire.
تنور (tannur): Oven used for baking bread.
الأجير المشترك (al-ajir al-mushtarak): A common hireling (worker hired by the public, not exclusively for one person) who is considered an amanah in his hands but liable for negligence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a baker bakes bread in the customer's house and it burns after removal, according to the text, what is the ruling?
A) He gets no wage and no liability.
B) He gets wage and no liability.
C) He gets wage and is liable.
D) No wage but liability.

Key Takeaway
A baker's wage is due upon actual delivery; location determines liability for loss after removal.

Cook's Wage Entitlement After Serving
Ruling on wage entitlement point for hired cook based on custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a cook becomes entitled to his wage and explain the preferred scope of the ruling (all food vs. wedding feasts only).

Core Idea
A cook's wage becomes due upon serving food into dishes, not upon consumption, and this applies to all hired cooking, not just weddings.

This lesson examines the moment of wage entitlement in a hired cook's contract. According to the Hanafi school, the cook's right to payment crystallizes when he places the food into serving bowls, as this is considered the completion of his work by custom. You will also encounter a disagreement within the school about whether this rule is restricted to wedding feasts or applies universally.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
State the act (cook being hired) and the ruling (wage wajib after gharf).
2
Locate the custom-based reasoning
Understand that the definition of 'completion' is based on custom (urf). The moment of serving into dishes is the point of delivery.
3
Note the restricted view of al-Quduri
Al-Quduri limited the ruling to wedding feast food only. Consider the basis for this restriction.
4
Identify the expanded view and its basis
Al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah and the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq extend it to all food. Why? Because the custom of serving into bowls is general.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The preferred opinion for fatwa is the general application. Cite the tarjih authority: al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وللطباخ بعد الغرف أي بعد وضع الطعام في القصاع اعتباراً للعرف. أطلقه فشمل كل طعام كما أطلقه في الفتاوى الظهيرية، وقيده القدوري بأن يكون طعام الوليمة. قال في قوله: (فأفاد أنه لو كان الخبز في بيت المستأجر فاحترق الخ أقول في الجامع الصغير وشروحه : أطلقوا الجواب بعدم الضمان ولم يذكروا الخلاف فعن هذا قالوا: الجواب مجرى على عمومه فعنده لا ضمان من صنعه، وأما عندهما فلأنه هلك بعد التسليم وإنما ذكر الخلاف القدوري البحر الرائق ج۷/ م ٣٣
He said: (And for the cook, after scooping) i.e., after placing the food into the bowls, considering custom. He gave it generally, so it includes all food as he gave it in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah, and al-Quduri restricted it to being wedding feast food. He said in his saying: (So it indicates that if the bread was in the lessee's house and burned ...) I say in al-Jami' al-Saghir and its commentaries: they gave the answer with no liability generally and did not mention the dispute, so from this they said: the answer proceeds on its generality; according to him (Abu Hanifa) no liability for his work; but according to the two (Sahibayn) because it perished after delivery; and al-Quduri mentioned the dispute. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq vol.7 p.33.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage discusses when a cook hired for a feast or other event becomes entitled to his wage. The ruling is that the wage becomes due after he places the food into bowls (gharf), which is the completion of his work according to custom. The commentator notes that al-Quduri restricted this ruling to wedding feasts, but al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah and the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (the commentator himself) hold it applies to all types of food. The passage then includes a note clarifying that the earlier ruling about the baker (no liability for burning after removal in lessee's house) is general according to al-Jami' al-Saghir, and the dispute with the two disciples is mentioned by al-Quduri but not in al-Jami' al-Saghir.

Key Terms
طباخ (tabbakh): Cook hired to prepare and serve food.
غرف (gharf): Scooping or serving food into bowls/plates.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, when does a cook hired for a general event become entitled to his wage?
A) Only after the guests have finished eating.
B) After placing the food into serving bowls (gharf).
C) At the end of the event.
D) Only if it is a wedding feast.

Key Takeaway
A cook's wage becomes wajib upon placing food into serving dishes, and this ruling applies to all cooking, not just wedding feasts.

Baker's Wage Entitlement Upon Removal from Oven
Ruling on baker's wage and liability after removal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the baker is entitled to wages and exempt from liability after removing bread from the oven, and explain the role of custom in determining completion of work.

Core Idea
The baker earns his wage upon removal; custom defines completion.

This lesson examines a concise ruling from the Hanafi matn regarding the hired baker. The text establishes a clear boundary: once the baker removes the bread from the oven, his work is considered complete. Even if the bread subsequently burns, he is entitled to his wage and bears no liability. The ruling is anchored in the custom (urf) of the time, which regarded removal as effective delivery. Understanding this point clarifies how Hanafi fiqh uses trade-specific custom to determine when a hired worker's obligation ends and his wage becomes due.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is the baker removing bread from the oven. The ruling: he receives his wage (ajr) and has no liability (daman) if the bread burns afterwards.
2
Note the Key Condition
The condition that triggers wage entitlement is the removal (ikhraj) of the bread. The text emphasizes 'after removing' (بعد إخراج), making removal the operative moment.
3
Understand the Role of Custom
The phrase 'This is according to their custom' (وهذا في عرفهم) grounds the ruling in trade practice. In the baker's context, removal from the oven constitutes delivery and completion of work, not physical handover to the owner.
Custom (urf) in Hanafi fiqh can define the terms of a hire contract when not explicitly stated.
4
Apply to Similar Trades
Different trades have different points of completion. For a tailor, work is complete upon delivery of the garment; for a baker, it is removal. Always consider the specific custom of the trade.
This prevents incorrectly analogizing one trade's ruling to another.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللخباز بعد إخراج الخبز من التنور فإن أخرجه فاحترق له الأجر ولا ضمان عليه وهذا في عرفهم
For the baker, after removing the bread from the oven, if he removes it and it burns, he is entitled to wages and no liability upon him. This is according to their custom.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn about the hired baker (ajir mushtarak). It establishes that the baker becomes entitled to his wage as soon as he removes the bread from the oven, even if the bread subsequently burns after removal. This is because removal (ikhraj) completes the work (tamam al-‘amal). The baker has no liability for the burning since no negligence is attributed to him; the bread is considered delivered to the owner upon removal. The phrase 'according to their custom' indicates that this ruling is based on the prevailing custom in their time. Some later scholars note that in later custom, the thread for sewing is provided by the garment owner, but that pertains to the tailor. The key point is that the baker's work is complete upon removal.

Key Terms
خباز (khabbaz): A baker hired to bake dough, an ajir mushtarak (shared worker) in the Hanafi classification.
أجر (ajr): The wage or compensation owed to the hired worker for his labor.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guaranty for loss or damage; here the baker is not liable for the bread after removal.
عرف (urf): Custom or common practice that influences legal rulings, especially in hiring contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, when does the baker become entitled to wages?
A) After kneading the dough
B) After removing the bread from the oven
C) After the owner receives the bread
D) After the bread is sold

Key Takeaway
The baker's wage is earned and his liability ceases upon removal of the bread from the oven, based on custom.

Tailor's Wage When Garment is Torn Before Delivery
Ruling on tailor's wage when garment is torn before delivery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a tailor's entitlement to wages when a third party damages the garment before delivery, and distinguish it from scenarios where the tailor himself causes the damage or dies after cutting.

Core Idea
Damage before delivery voids the wage; the tailor's own damage requires redoing.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a common fiqh question: what happens to a tailor's wages if the garment is torn before the owner takes possession? The ruling depends on who caused the damage. Understanding this distinction is crucial for anyone engaging in or contracting for hired work (ijarah), as it clarifies liability and entitlement when work is not fully delivered.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the work
The scenario involves a tailor (ajir mushtarak) hired to sew a garment for wages. The work is sewing (khayatah).
The tailor is a common hireling, not a specific hireling.
2
Determine the timing of damage
Damage occurs before the owner takes possession of the sewn garment. This is key.
Possession here means physical delivery to the owner.
3
Apply the ruling for third-party damage
If a third party tears the garment, the tailor loses his wage and is not forced to resew. The third party may be liable for damages, but that compensation goes to the tailor (to offset lost wage).
The tailor is not liable for the third party's act.
4
Apply the ruling for tailor's own damage
If the tailor himself tears the garment, he must redo the work without additional pay, as if he had never sewn.
His own negligence or mistake nullifies the completed work.
5
Consider the case of cutting by a tailor who dies
If the tailor only cuts the cloth and then dies, no wage is due because the wage is for sewing, not cutting. Cutting alone is not the primary work.
Custom (urf) determines that sewing is the compensated work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المخيط الخياط إذا خاطه بأجر ففتقه رجل قبل أن يقبضه رب الثوب فلا أجر للخياط ولا يجبر على الإعادة، وإن كان الخياط هو الذي فتقه فعليه الإعادة كأنه لم يعمل بخلاف ما إذا فتقه الأجنبي ألا يلزمه الضمان وفي الخياط لا يلزمه اهـ. ولا يخفى أن ما ضمنه الأجنبي يكون للخياط لكونه بدل ما أتلفه عليه حتى سقطت أجرته. وفي الخلاصة رجل دفع إلى خياط ثوباً ليخيطه فقطعه ومات لا يجب شيء من الأجرة لأن الأجر في العادة للخياطة لا للقطع وهو الأصح اهـ.
And regarding the sewn garment: the tailor, if he sews it for wages and a man tears it before the garment's owner takes possession, then there is no wage for the tailor and he is not forced to redo it. But if the tailor himself tears it, he must redo it, as if he had not worked. This is unlike the case when an outsider tears it, who is not liable for guarantee? And the tailor is not liable. It is not hidden that what the outsider guarantees becomes for the tailor because it is compensation for what he destroyed, until his wage is dropped. And in al-Khulasah: a man gave a garment to a tailor to sew it, and he cut it and died; no wage is due because the wage is customarily for sewing, not for cutting, and this is more correct.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings related to the tailor. First, if a tailor sews a garment for wages and a third party tears the garment before delivery to the owner, the tailor loses his wage and is not required to resew it. This is because the work is considered incomplete due to the damage, and the tailor is not responsible for the third party's act. However, if the tailor himself tears the garment, he must redo the work, as if he never performed it, because his own act caused the damage. The second ruling from al-Khulasah concerns a tailor who cuts the cloth (presumably to sew) and then dies; no wage is due because the wage is customarily for the completed sewing, not for the cutting alone. The cutting is not the primary work.

Key Terms
خياط (khayyat): A tailor, one who sews garments for hire, considered an ajir mushtarak.
فتقه (fataqahu): He tore it or ripped it apart, rendering the sewn garment damaged.
إعادة (i'adah): Redoing the work; the tailor is compelled to redo if he caused the damage.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee; the outsider may be liable to compensate, but the tailor does not guarantee the work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a tailor sews a garment for wages and a third party tears it before the owner takes it, what is the tailor's liability?
A) He must resew it without extra pay
B) He loses his wage and is not required to resew
C) He keeps his wage and the third party pays damages
D) He must pay for the torn garment

Key Takeaway
Damage to the sewn garment before delivery by a third party frees the tailor from both wage obligation and duty to redo.

When No Fee is Specified: The Washer's Wage in Hanafi Fiqh
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wage in unspecified hiring

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the washer's wage when no fee is specified, and apply the mufta bihi view that custom establishes the wage.

Core Idea
Custom substitutes for explicit wage: the washer's wage becomes wajib if he customarily works for wages.

In hiring contracts, what happens if the wage is not mentioned at the outset? This passage from al-Fatawa al-Sughra presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on the washer (qassar). Abu Hanifa holds that without an agreed fee, no wage is due. Muhammad al-Shaybani introduces custom as a determining factor: if the washer is established in his profession and customarily accepts work for wages, then he is entitled to payment. The later school authorities adopt Muhammad's view, demonstrating the Hanafi reliance on 'urf (custom) in contractual obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their positions
Read the source: Abu Hanifa says 'no wage'; Muhammad says 'wage if established customarily'. Note the basis of disagreement.
Abu Hanifa requires explicit mention of wage for a valid hiring; Muhammad allows custom to fill the gap.
2
Understand the operative condition: intisab
The key term is 'intasaba' — the washer has set himself up in the profession such that people customarily hire him for wages. This is the condition that triggers the obligation.
Customary practice establishes an implicit agreement.
3
Identify the source and the fatwa
The passage is from al-Fatawa al-Sughra, not the Zahir al-Riwayah. The author of al-Khulasah, citing al-Sadr al-Shahid, states that the fatwa (relied-upon opinion) is on Muhammad's view.
This is an example of later Hanafi authority selecting one of two valid positions.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider: A man gives his garment to a washer without discussing payment. If the washer is known in that area to do such work for wages, he must be paid the customary wage. If he is not, no payment is due.
The ruling hinges on the washer's professional reputation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الفتاوى الصغرى : إذا دفع ثوباً لقصار ليقصره ولم يسم له أجراً قال أبو حنيفة : لا أجر له. وقال محمد: إن انتصب القصار لقبول ذلك من الناس بالأجر كما وإلا فلا. قال في الخلاصة معزياً إلى الصدر الشهيد والفتوى على قول محمد
And in al-Fatawa al-Sughra: If a man gives a garment to a washer (qassar) to wash it and does not specify a fee for him, Abu Hanifa said: There is no wage for him. And Muhammad said: If the washer is established (to accept that) from people for wages, then [he gets wages]; otherwise, no. He said in al-Khulasah, citing al-Sadr al-Shahid: The fatwa is upon the saying of Muhammad.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the washer (qassar), a hired worker who cleans clothes. Abu Hanifa holds that if no fee is mentioned at the time of hiring, no wage is due because the contract is incomplete. Muhammad al-Shaybani distinguishes based on custom: if the washer is known to accept such work for wages customarily, he is entitled to wages even without explicit mention; if not, no wage is due. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to al-Khulasah and al-Sadr al-Shahid is the view of Muhammad, giving weight to custom ('urf) in determining wages.

Key Terms
قصار (qassar): A washer or launderer, one who washes clothes for hire.
أجر (ajr): Wage or fee for the service.
انتصب (intasaba): He set himself established himself in that profession; customarily accepts such work.
الفتوى (al-fatwa): The legal opinion that is relied upon and practiced.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in this text, what is the ruling on the washer's wage if no fee was specified?
A) No wage at all
B) Wage is due if the washer customarily does such work for wages
C) The washer gets the market rate regardless
D) The owner decides the wage

Key Takeaway
Custom validates the wage in an unspecified hiring: if the worker customarily works for wages, payment is obligatory.

Detailed Ruling on Baker's Liability When Bread Burns After Removal
Commentary on baker's wage and liability including differences among Abu Hanifa and the two companions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the baker's liability when bread burns after removal and explain the intra-madhhab disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the two companions.

Core Idea
After delivery, baker is liability-free by consensus; before delivery, liability depends on location and negligence.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a critical point in Ijarah: what happens if the baker removes bread from the oven and it burns? The ruling hinges on where the burning occurs and whether delivery has taken place. The text first establishes a consensus (ijma) on no liability after delivery, then presents a dispute among the Hanafi imams regarding bread that burns in the baker's house.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being judged (removing bread) and the ruling (wage and liability status).
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites 'إجماعاً' (consensus) as proof for no liability after delivery.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the consensus proves that delivery (taslim) ends liability.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
When bread burns in baker's house, Abu Hanifa says no wage and no liability; the two companions give the hirer an option.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference lies in the hirer's ability to choose compensation (flour vs. value) and wage entitlement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن أخرجه فاحترق فله الأجر ولا ضمان عليه لأنه صار مسلماً بالوضع في بيته فأستحق المسمى ولم يوجد منه جناية فلا ضمان عليه إجماعاً فأفاد أنه لو كان الخبز في غير بيت المستأجر فاحترق فلا أجر له ولا ضمان عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما إن شاء ضمنه دقيقاً مثل دقيقه ولا أجر له وإن شاء ضمنه قيمة الخبز وأعطاه الأجر ولا يجب عليه ضمان الحطب والملح. وقيد بكونه احترق عقيب الإخراج لأنه إذا احترق قبل الإخراج فعليه الضمان في قول أصحابنا جميعاً لأنه مما جنته يداه بتقصيره في القلع من التنور فإن ضمنه قيمته مخبوزاً أعطاه الأجر، وإن ضمنه دقيقاً لم يكن له أجر ؛ كذا في غاية البيان
His saying: (For if he removes it and it burns, he is entitled to wages and no liability upon him) because it became delivered by placing in his house, so he becomes entitled to the named wage, and no offense is found from him, so no liability upon him by consensus. So it indicates that if the bread was in a place other than the hirer's house and it burned, then there is no wage and no liability according to Abu Hanifa. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if he wishes he compensates it with flour like his flour and no wage for him, and if he wishes he compensates the value of the bread and gives him the wage, and he is not obliged to compensate for the firewood and salt. And it is conditioned that it burns immediately after removal because if it burns before removal, he is liable according to all our companions because it is an act of his hands due to his negligence in removing from the oven. Then if he compensates its value as baked, he gives him the wage, and if he compensates it as flour, there is no wage for him. As in Ghayat al-Bayan.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This commentary on the earlier matn explains that the baker gets wage and no liability by consensus (ijma) when bread burns in the hirer's house after removal. The dispute arises when bread burns in a location other than the hirer's house (e.g., the baker's house): Abu Hanifa says no wage and no liability; the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) give the hirer an option: either take compensation in flour (like his flour) and give no wage, or take the value of baked bread and give the wage. The worker is not liable for firewood and salt. The condition 'immediately after removal' is crucial: if the bread burns before removal, the baker is liable because he was negligent in removing it. In that case, if he compensates with baked value, he gets wage; if with flour, no wage.

Key Terms
مسلماً (musallaman): Delivered or handed over; the bread is considered delivered to the hirer.
مسمى (musamma): The named or agreed wage specified in the contract.
جناية (jinayah): An offense or act of aggression causing damage; absence of such means no liability.
إجماعاً (ijma'an): By consensus of the scholars, a source of law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if bread burns after removal from the oven but in the baker's house, what is the ruling?
A) The baker gets wage and is liable
B) The baker gets no wage and is not liable
C) The baker gets no wage but is liable
D) The baker gets wage and is not liable

Key Takeaway
Baker's liability depends on delivery and location of burning; after delivery in hirer's house, no liability by consensus.

Cook's Entitlement to Wages and Liability
Ruling on when the cook becomes entitled to wages based on custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a hired cook becomes entitled to wages and explain the Hanafi dispute regarding the scope of the ruling, and apply the liability rules for accidental fire.

Core Idea
A cook earns wages by serving food into dishes, based on custom, and is liable for spoilage but not for permitted fire.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a practical issue in hiring (ijara): when does the cook's entitlement to wages crystallize? The text relies on custom ('urf) to determine the moment of completion. It also navigates an internal Hanafi disagreement: al-Quduri restricted the ruling to wedding feasts, but the author of al-Hidayah generalized it. Additionally, liability rules for damage to food or property are provided, distinguishing between culpable negligence and permitted actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the moment of entitlement
The cook becomes entitled to wages after serving the food into bowls (gharafa), based on custom. The text says 'بعد الغرف' i.e., after placing food into dishes.
Custom ('urf) is the basis – not eating or other milestones.
2
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Al-Quduri restricted the ruling to wedding feasts (walimah), but the author of al-Hidayah generalized it to all food. The text supports the general view by listing various feasts.
The dispute is about scope: only walimah or all food.
3
Note the exceptions
Food prepared for the cook's own family is excluded because customarily no hired cook is needed.
4
Analyze liability for spoilage
If the cook spoils, burns, or undercooks the food, he is liable (daman) because he is an ajir mushtarak and his work is defective.
Liability arises from negligence or breach of contract.
5
Analyze liability for accidental fire
If the cook or baker brings fire with permission and a spark causes a fire, there is no liability because he is permitted to bring the fire. Similarly, the homeowner is not liable for damage to tenants from fire if not negligent.
This is based on analogy with digging a well on one's own property – no liability if not transgressing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وللطباخ بعد الغرف) أي بعد وضع الطعام في القصاع اعتباراً للعرف. أطلقه فشمل كل طعام كما أطلقه في الفتاوى الظهيرية، وقيده القدوري بأن يكون طعام الوليمة. قال في الجوهرة : إذ لو كان لأهل بيته فلا غرف عليه .اهـ. وإنما لم يقيده المصنف لأنه به يرد عليه بقية أنواع الأطعمة فإن الوليمة طعام العرس والوكيرة طعام البناء، والخرس طعام الولادة، وما تطعم النفساء نفسها خرسة وطعام الختام إعذار وطعام القادم من سفره نقيعة، وكل طعام صنع لدعوة مأدبة ومادية جميعاً ويقال فلان يدعو النقرى إذا خص، وفلان يدعو الجفلى عم، في غاية البيان معزياً إلى القتبي. ولا يرد على المصنف طعام أهل بيته لأن العرف أنه لا يحتاج إلى طباخ وإن أفسد الطباخ الطعام أو أحرقه أو لم ينضجه فهو ضامن، وإذا دخل الخباز أو الطباخ بنار ليخبز بها أو يطبخ بها فوقعت منه شرارة فاحترق بها البيت فلا ضمان عليه لأنه لم يصل إلى العمل إلا بإدخال النار وهو مأذون له في ذلك، ولا ضمان على صاحب الدار إذا احترق شيء من السكان في الدار لأنه لم يكن متعدياً في السبب كمن حفر بئراً في ملكه ؛ كذا في الجوهرة
His saying: (And for the cook, after serving) i.e., after placing the food into bowls, considering custom. He gave it absolutely, so it includes all food, as he gave it absolutely in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah, and al-Quduri restricted it to being the food of a wedding feast. He said in al-Jawhara: If it was for his own family, then there is no serving upon him. The author did not restrict it only to wedding feast because various types of food would be excluded: al-walimah is the food of a wedding, al-wakiarah is food of building, al-khurs is food of childbirth, and what the woman in nifas feeds herself is khursa, and the food of completion [of the Quran?] is idhar, and the food of the traveler returning from his trip is naqi'ah. And every food made for an invitation is ma'dabah and madiyyah. And it is said that such-and-such invites for a specific group (al-naqra) and such-and-such invites generally (al-jafal). In Ghayat al-Bayan citing al-Qutaybi. And the author is not refuted regarding the food of his own family because custom is that he does not need a cook. And if the cook spoils the food, or burns it, or does not cook it, then he is liable. And if the baker or cook enters with fire to bake or cook with it, and a spark falls and burns the house, there is no liability upon him because he doesn't proceed to the work except by bringing in the fire, and he is permitted to do so. And there is no liability upon the owner of the house if something of the inhabitants burns in the house because he was not transgressing in the cause, like one who digs a well in his property. As in al-Jawhara.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage discusses when the hired cook becomes entitled to wages. According to the text, the cook earns his wage after serving the food into dishes (ghurfa), based on custom. The ruling is general and applies to all types of food, not limited to wedding feasts as al-Quduri opined. Various types of feasts are enumerated. Importantly, food prepared for the cook's own family is excluded because customarily no hired cook is needed. The passage also covers liability: if the cook spoils the food, he is liable for damages. However, if a baker or cook brings fire into the premises and accidentally causes a fire, there is no liability because he is permitted to bring the fire. Similarly, the homeowner is not liable for damage to tenants' property from fire unless he was negligent, analogized to digging a well on one's own property.

Key Terms
طباخ (tabbakh): A cook hired to prepare food for an event, an ajir mushtarak.
غرف (gharafa): Serving the food into bowls or dishes; the moment at which the cook's work is deemed complete.
وليمة (walimah): The wedding feast, specifically the meal served at a wedding.
ضمان (daman): Liability; the cook is liable if he spoils the food, but not for accidental fire if permitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, when does the hired cook become entitled to his wage?
A) After the guests finish eating
B) After the food is cooked
C) After serving the food into bowls
D) After the host pays him

Key Takeaway
The cook's wage is wajib upon serving food into bowls, based on custom, and he is not liable for permitted acts like bringing fire.

When Does a Bricklayer Earn His Wage? The Hanafi Dispute on Completion
Intra-Hanafi dispute on completion of brickmaking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on when a bricklayer becomes entitled to wages, identify the thamarah al-khilaf regarding destruction, and apply the ruling to similar hire cases.

Core Idea
A bricklayer's wage is due upon completion; the dispute is whether completion is setting or stacking — and liability for loss hinges on that.

When you hire a bricklayer to make bricks, when exactly does he earn his wage? Abu Hanifa and his two companions disagreed on the point of completion. This lesson unpacks their arguments and the practical consequences, such as who bears the loss if the bricks are destroyed before stacking. We'll also see how location and custom affect the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is hiring a person to strike (make) bricks. The dispute: when does the worker become entitled to wages?
The key terms are iqamah (setting bricks upright to dry) and tashrij (stacking them after drying).
2
State Abu Hanifa’s position and proof
Abu Hanifa says wage is due after iqamah. His proof: the work is completed by setting; stacking is an extra service like transport. The bricks are usable (can be moved) after setting.
He analogizes to bread: removing from oven is completion; stacking is not needed.
3
State the two companions’ position and proof
The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say wage is due only after tashrij. Their proof: stacking is part of completing the work because bricks are prone to damage before stacking, similar to removing bread from the oven.
They consider iqamah alone insufficient; the bricks are still vulnerable.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If the bricks are destroyed before stacking but after setting, Abu Hanifa says it is the hirer's loss (wage due), while the companions say it is the worker's loss (no wage). If destroyed before setting, all agree no wage is due.
This is the key practical difference: who bears the risk of loss?
5
Consider location and delivery conditions
If the work is in the hirer's property, delivery occurs by setting/stacking. If in the worker's property, additional delivery by counting is required according to each view. Counting is preferred for entitlement.
Custom (urf) plays a role in determining when delivery is complete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وللبان بعد الإقامة) يعني من استأجر إنساناً ليضرب له لبناً استحق الأجر إذا أقامه عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : لا يستحقها حتى يشرجه لأن التشريج من تمام عمله إذ لا يؤمن من الفساد قبله فصار كالإخراج من التنور. وله أن العمل قد تم بالإقامة والتشريج عمل زائد كالنقل ألا ترى أنه ينتفع به قبل التشريج بالنقل إلى موضع العمل بخلاف ما قبل الإقامة لأنه طين منتشر وبخلاف الخبز لأنه غير منتفع به قبل الإخراج وفائدة الخلاف فيما إذا تلف اللبن قبل التشريج فعند أبي حنيفة من مال المستأجر. وعندهما من مال الأجير . وأما إذا تلف قبل الإقامة فلا أجرة إجماعاً . ومراده ما إذا كان ضرب اللبن في بيت المستأجر أما إذا كان في أرض الأجير فلا يستحقها إلا بتسليمه وهو بالعد بعد الإقامة عنده، وبالعد بعد التشريج عندهما؛ كذا ذكر الشارح . وعبارة المصنف في المستصفى : فأما إذا لم يكن في ملکه لم يكن له الأجر حتى يسلمه منصوباً عنده ومشرجاً عندهما كذا في الإيضاح والمبسوط .اهـ. فلم يشترط العد وهو الأولى لأنه لو سلمه بغير عد كان له الأجر كما لا يخفى والإقامة النصف بعد الجفاف، والتشريج أن يركب بعضه على بعض بعد الجفاف؛ كذا في الجوهرة. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان والظهيرية : الملبن على اللبان والتراب على المستأجر، وإدخال الحمل المنزل على الحمال ولا يكون عليه يصعد به على السطح أو الغرفة إلا أن يشترط ذلك عليه، وكذلك صب الطعام في الجفنة لا يكون عليه إلا بشرط ولو تكارى دابة ليحمل عليها صاحب الدابة الحمل فإنزال الحمل عن الدابة يكون على المكاري وإدخال الحمل في المنزل لا يكون عليه إلا أن يكون في
His saying: (And for the bricklayer, after setting [the bricks]) meaning: If a man hires a person to strike bricks for him, he becomes entitled to wages when he sets them (aqamahu) according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He does not become entitled until he stacks them (yusharrij) because stacking is part of completing his work since there is no guarantee against corruption before that, so it becomes like removal from the oven. And for him (Abu Hanifa), the work is completed with setting, and stacking is an extra work like transport. Do you not see that he can benefit from it before stacking by transporting to the workplace, unlike before setting because it is scattered clay, and unlike bread because it is not beneficial before removal. And the practical consequence of the dispute is regarding when the bricks are destroyed before stacking: according to Abu Hanifa, it is from the hirer's property; according to the two, from the worker's property. And if destroyed before setting, there is no wage by consensus. And his meaning is when the brick-striking is in the hirer's house; but if in the worker's land, he does not become entitled except by delivery, which is by counting after setting according to him, and by counting after stacking according to them. As the commentator mentioned. And the author's phrase in al-Mustasfa: But if it is not in his property, he has no wage until he delivers it set up according to him, and stacked according to them. As in al-Idah and al-Mabsut. He did not stipulate counting, and that is preferable because if he delivers it without counting, he is entitled to wages as is obvious. And setting (iqamah) is when the bricks stand after drying; stacking (tashrij) is when one piles some on others after drying. As in al-Jawhara. And in Fatawa Qadikhan and al-Zahiriyyah: The bricks belong to the bricklayer, and the soil belongs to the hirer. Bringing down the load into the house is on the porter, but climbing to the roof or room is not on him unless stipulated. Similarly, pouring food into the bowl is not on him unless stipulated. And if one hires a donkey to carry a load, the owner of the donkey is to load, and bringing down the load from the donkey is on the hirer, and bringing the load into the house is not on him unless it is in...
Source pages p. 514

Commentary
This passage covers the bricklayer (laban) who makes bricks. According to Abu Hanifa, the hired worker becomes entitled to wages once he sets the bricks upright to dry (iqamah). According to the two companions, he must also stack them (tashrij) because the bricks may still be prone to damage before stacking. Abu Hanifa views stacking as an additional service like transport, since the bricks are already usable for transport after setting. The practical consequence (thamara) is that if the bricks are destroyed before stacking, Abu Hanifa considers it the hirer's loss (since the worker completed his work), while the two consider it the worker's loss (since work not complete). If destroyed before setting, all agree no wage. The location matters: if the work is in the hirer's property, delivery occurs by setting/stacking; if in the worker's property, additional delivery by counting is required. The passage also includes related rulings about loading, porters, and food serving, derived from customs and other fatwa sources.

Key Terms
لبان (laban): Bricklayer or brickmaker; one who forms and dries bricks for hire.
إقامة (iqamah): Setting the bricks upright to dry after formation; considered completion by Abu Hanifa.
تشريج (tashrij): Stacking dried bricks together; considered necessary for completion by the two companions.
تلف (talaf): Destruction or loss of the bricks before delivery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) After mixing the clay
B) After setting the bricks upright
C) After stacking the bricks
D) After the hirer inspects them

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on when a bricklayer's wage is due: after setting (Abu Hanifa) or after stacking (companions), affecting liability for loss.

Right of Retention for Workers with a Trace
Ruling on worker's right to withhold for wage, with definition of athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a worker's right to withhold the object for his wage, identify which workers have this right based on the presence of a trace (athar), and apply the conditions for valid retention.

Core Idea
Only workers whose labor leaves a trace in the object may withhold it for their wage; those without trace become usurpers if they do.

The right to retain possession of a customer's property until payment is a common security mechanism in service contracts. Hanafi fiqh carefully restricts this right to workers whose labor actually becomes part of the object, such as dyers and fullers. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind this rule, its conditions, and the internal disagreements within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and general ruling
The passage rules that a worker whose work leaves a trace (athar) in the object may withhold the object from the hirer until his wage is paid. Note the key terms: 'athar' (trace) and 'habsh' (retention).
The right is based on the analogy to a seller withholding the sold item for the price.
2
Locate the proof (dalil) for the ruling
The proof is that the subject matter of the ijara contract is a quality that becomes part of the object (e.g., dye in cloth), similar to the item in a sale. Therefore, the worker has a right to retain the object until he receives the substitute (wage).
This is an argument by qiyas (analogy) to sale.
3
Identify the conditions for the right of retention
The passage mentions two conditions: (1) the wage must be payable immediately (halan); if deferred, no retention. (2) The work must be done in the worker's own premises (house or shop); if done on the hirer's premises, the object is already in the hirer's possession and retention is not possible.
If the worker withholds despite these conditions, he may become a usurper (ghasib).
4
Analyze the internal ikhtilaf on liability if the object perishes
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if the object perishes while rightfully withheld, the worker has no wage and no liability because he is not a transgressor. The two companions (Sahibayn) argue the object was guaranteed from the start of work, so the worker is liable unless the hirer chooses to pay wage and take the worked object.
This disagreement has practical consequences for the hirer's options.
5
Evaluate the dispute on the definition of 'athar'
Two definitions: (1) the trace must be inherent and connected to the object (e.g., dye, saw marks). (2) the trace can be any visible effect (e.g., broken wood, ground grain). The text notes that al-Qunyah prefers the second, but the school's reasoning favors the first, as the subject of the contract is a quality in the substance.
This dispute affects whether a woodcutter or grinder can withhold.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ومن لعمله أثر في العين كالصباغ والقصار يحبسهما للاجر) لأن المعقود عليه وصف قائم في الثوب فله حق الحبس لاستيفاء البدل كما في المبيع. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا لم يكن لعمله إلا إزالة الدرن بالغسل فقط على الأصح لأن البياض كان مستتراً وقد ظهر بفعله فكأنه أحدثه فيه؛ كذا ذكر قاضيخان في شرحه، وصححه المصنف في مستصفاه معزياً إلى الذخيرة أن ليس له حق الحبس فاختلف التصحيح وينبغي ترجيح المنع، وقد جزم به صاحب الهداية بقوله : وغسل الثوب نظير الحمل. ومراده إذا كان الأجر حالاً، أما إذا كان مؤجلاً فليس له الحبس عليها لأن التسليم ليس بواجب عليه للحال فلا يملك الحبس كما لو باع شيئاً بثمن مؤجل ليس له الحبس. وأشار بقوله «يحبسه» إلى أنه عمله في بيته أو دكانه فأفاد أنه إذا خاطه أو صبغه في بيت المستأجر فليس له حق الحبس لأن المتاع وقع مسلماً إلى المالك لكون المحل في يده ؛ كذا في الخلاصة وهو ضامن لما جنت يده عند الإمام وإن كان في بيت المستأجر بخلاف الملاح إذا غرقت السفينة بمده وصاحب المتاع فيها حيث لا يضمن المتاع لأنه في يد مالكه حقيقة والمد تصرف في السفية دون المتاع فمتى كان مأذوناً فيه من قبل المالك لم يكن متعدياً في السبب فلا يؤاخذ بالضمان؛ كذا في غاية البيان قوله : (فإن حبس فضاع فلا أجر ولا ضمان) وهذا عند الإمام لأنه غير متعد في الحبس فبقي أمانة كما كان عنده، ولا أجر له الهلاك المعقود عليه قبل التسليم وعندهما العين كانت مضمونة قبل الحبس فكذا بعده لكنه بالخيار إن شاء ضمنه غير معمول ولا أجر له، وإن شاء معمولاً وله الأجر قوله : ( ومن لا أثر لعمله كالحمال والملاح لا يحبس للأجر) لأن المعقود عليه نفس العمل وهو غير قائم في العين فلا يتصور حبسه فليس له ولاية الحبس فأفاد أنه لو حبسها ضمنها ضمان الغاصب وصاحبها بالخيار إن شاء ضمنه قيمتها محمولة وله الأجر، وإن شاء غير محمولة فلا أجر له ؛ كذا في الجوهرة. واختلفوا في المراد من الأثر فقيل أن تكون الأثرة متصلة بمحل العمل كالنشار ،والصبغ وقيل أن يرى ويعاين في محل العمل، وثمرته تظهر في كسر الحطب وطحن الحنطة وحلق رأس العبد فليس له الحبس على الأول، وله الحبس على الثاني. وظاهر ما في القنية ترجيح الثاني، والذي يظهر من كلامهم ترجيح الأول لما عللوا به في حق الحبس من أن المعقود عليه وصف في الثوب ومنهم من ضبط الحمال بالحاء المهملة، ومنهم من ضبطها بالجيم والأولى His saying: (And for the one whose work has a trace in the substance, like the dyer and fuller, he may withhold them for the wage) because the subject matter of the contract is a quality subsisting in the cloth, so he has the right of retention to obtain the substitute as in a sale. He made it absolute, so it includes if his work was only removing dirt by washing, on the most correct view, because the whiteness was hidden and has appeared by his action, so it is as if he created it in it; as Qadikhan mentioned in his commentary. And the author corrected in his Mustasfa, attributing to al-Dhakhira, that he has no right of retention, so correction conflicts, and it is appropriate to prefer the prohibition, and the author of al-Hidayah affirmed it by his saying: washing cloth is similar to carrying. His intent is when the wage is payable immediately (halan); if it is deferred (mu'ajjalan), he does not have retention because delivery is not obligatory on him immediately, so he does not own retention, as if he sold something with deferred price he has no retention. And by his saying 'he may withhold' he indicated that his work is in his house or shop; so it follows that if he sewed or dyed in the hirer's house, he has no right of retention because the goods are delivered to the owner as the place is in his hand; as in al-Khulasa. And he is liable for what his hand injured according to Imam, even if in the hirer's house, unlike the boatman if the ship sinks by his pull and the owner of goods is on it, he does not guarantee the goods because it is truly in the owner's hand, and the pull is an action on the ship not on the goods, so if he is authorized by the owner, he is not transgressing in the cause, so he is not taken to liability; as in Ghayat al-Bayan. His saying: (And if he withholds and it perishes, there is no wage and no liability) and this is according to Imam because he is not transgressing in the retention, so it remains a trust as before him, and he has no wage for the destruction of the contracted subject matter before delivery, while according to the two (companions) the object was guaranteed before retention, so likewise after, but he has a choice: if he wishes, he guarantees it not worked, and no wage; or if he wishes, worked, and he has wage. His saying: (And the one whose work has no trace, like the porter and boatman, he does not withhold for the wage) because the subject matter of the contract is the work itself, which does not subsist in the object, so retention cannot be conceived, so he has no authority to retain. So it follows that if he withholds it, he guarantees it as a usurper, and its owner has a choice: if he wishes, he guarantees its value as carried and he has wage; or if he wishes, not carried, so no wage; as in al-Jawhara. And they disagreed on the meaning of 'trace': it is said that the trace must be connected to the place of work, like sawing and dyeing; and it is said that it can be seen and observed in the place of work, and its fruit appears in breaking firewood, grinding wheat, and shaving a slave's head, so he has no retention according to the first, and he has retention according to the second. And what appears in al-Qunyah is a preference for the second, and what appears from their speech is a preference for the first due to their reasoning regarding retention that the subject matter is a quality in the cloth. And among them are those who spell al-hammal with imala, and among them are those who spell it with jim, and the first is better because al-haml (carrying) can occur on the back. His saying: (It is appropriate to prefer prohibition) al-Ramli said: This commentator presented in al-Qada that retention is in prohibition... perhaps it is appropriate to prefer non-prohibition, i.e., no retention for the object, so it is omitted from the author's line, or its meaning is preference.
Source pages p. 515

Commentary
This extensive passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the right of a hired worker to withhold (habsh) the object of his work for his wage. It categorizes workers based on whether their work leaves a trace (athar) in the object. Those whose work leaves a trace, like a dyer (sabbagh) or fuller (qassar), have the right to withhold the object (e.g., cloth) until their wage is paid. The reason is that the subject of the contract is a quality that becomes part of the object (e.g., dye), similar to a seller withholding a sold item for the price. This applies even if the work only involves cleaning, as the whiteness emerges through his effort. However, there is a disagreement: some authorities like Qadikhan say the cleaner has no right of retention, and the author of al-Hidayah equates washing cloth to carrying (which has no trace), so the correct view in the school is that such a worker cannot withhold (tarjih al-man'). The right of retention exists only if the wage is due immediately (halan); if deferred, there is no retention because the worker is not obliged to deliver immediately. Additionally, if the work is done on the hirer's premises, the worker cannot withhold because the object is already in the hirer's possession. The passage also addresses liability: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if the worker withholds the object and it perishes without his fault, he has no wage and no liability; according to the two companions, the object becomes guaranteed (mamnunah) from the start of work, so the worker can choose to guarantee it as unworked (no wage) or as worked (with wage). For workers with no trace, like a porter (hammal) or boatman (mallah), they cannot withhold at all because their work does not subsist in the object; if they do, they become usurpers and are liable. The passage concludes with a discussion on the definition of 'trace': some say it must be inherent and connected (like dye or sawdust), others say it's visible effect (like broken wood or milled grain). The preferred view in al-Qunyah is the second, but from the school's reasoning, the first seems more consistent because the subject of the contract is a quality in the substance. A note from al-Ramli clarifies a possible textual corruption in the phrase 'ترجيح المنع'.

Key Terms
أثر (athar): A trace or effect left by the worker's labor that becomes part of the object, such as dye, sewing, or cleaning that reveals whiteness.
حبس (habsh): The right of a worker to retain possession of the object of his work until his wage is paid.
ضمان الغاصب (ḍamān al-ghāṣib): Liability of a usurper; full compensation for the value of the object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following workers has the right to withhold the object of his work for his wage?
A) A porter (hammal)
B) A boatman (mallah)
C) A dyer (sabbagh)
D) A woodcutter (hattab)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi right of retention for wages is limited to workers whose labor leaves a lasting trace in the object, subject to conditions of immediate wage and work on the worker's premises.

Right of Detention for Workers with Trace vs. No Trace
Ruling on detention rights of ajir based on trace, with intra-madhhab dispute on liability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the ruling on detention for workers with and without trace, and DISTINGUISH the intra-Hanafi positions on liability after detention.

Core Idea
A worker whose work leaves a trace has a right of detention, but the preferred Hanafi view denies it.

This passage from the Bahr al-Raiq addresses a practical question in Ijara contracts: can a worker, such as a dyer or a porter, retain possession of the object until his wage is paid? The answer depends on whether the worker's work leaves a trace (athar) in the object. The text then delves into the implications of detention, including liability for loss, where the Imaman (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) disagree.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of workers
List workers whose work leaves a trace (like dyer, fuller) and those without (like porter, boatman). Note the key difference: the contracted benefit subsists in the object for the first group but not the second.
The trace can be adding color, stitching, or even revealing hidden whiteness by washing.
2
State the basic ruling for each type
For workers with trace, the base text (Kanz) says they may detain for the wage. For workers without trace, they have no right of detention.
The ruling for workers with trace is qualified: it applies only when the wage is immediate and work done in the worker's premises.
3
Analyze the proof for workers with trace
The proof is qiyas on sale: in sale, the seller may detain the sold item until payment because the contracted object (the item) subsists. Similarly, the worker's benefit (dye, stitching) subsists in the object, so he may detain.
The 'illa is the subsistence of the contracted benefit in the object.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi correction and tarjih
Although the base text affirms the right, later authorities like the author of al-Dhakhira and Ibn Nujaym prefer prohibition (man‘). They analogize washing cloth to carrying, which has no trace. The preferred view for fatwa is that even workers with trace cannot detain.
The tarjih is based on the harm of retaining another's property and the possibility of claiming wage through court.
5
Distinguish the liability positions if detention occurs
If the worker detains and the object is lost, Abu Hanifa holds he is not liable (no wage either) because detention is non-transgressory. The Sahibayn hold he is liable with an option to claim wage or not.
This dispute arises only if the worker had the right to detain; if not (as per tarjih), detention itself is transgression.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن لعمله أثر في العين كالصباغ والقصار يحبسهما للاجر) لأن المعقود عليه وصف قائم في الثوب فله حق الحبس لاستيفاء البدل كما في المبيع. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا لم يكن لعمله إلا إزالة الدرن بالغسل فقط على الأصح لأن البياض كان مستتراً وقد ظهر بفعله فكأنه أحدثه فيه؛ كذا ذكر قاضيخان في شرحه، وصححه المصنف في مستصفاه معزياً إلى الذخيرة أن ليس له حق الحبس فاختلف التصحيح وينبغي ترجيح المنع، وقد جزم به صاحب الهداية بقوله : وغسل الثوب نظير الحمل. ومراده إذا كان الأجر حالاً، أما إذا كان مؤجلاً فليس له الحبس عليها لأن التسليم ليس بواجب عليه للحال فلا يملك الحبس كما لو باع شيئاً بثمن مؤجل ليس له الحبس. وأشار بقوله «يحبسه» إلى أنه عمله في بيته أو دكانه فأفاد أنه إذا خاطه أو صبغه في بيت المستأجر فليس له حق الحبس لأن المتاع وقع مسلماً إلى المالك لكون المحل في يده ؛ كذا في الخلاصة وهو ضامن لما جنت يده عند الإمام وإن كان في بيت المستأجر بخلاف الملاح إذا غرقت السفينة بمده وصاحب المتاع فيها حيث لا يضمن المتاع لأنه في يد مالكه حقيقة والمد تصرف في السفية دون المتاع فمتى كان مأذوناً فيه من قبل المالك لم يكن متعدياً في السبب فلا يؤاخذ بالضمان؛ كذا في غاية البيان قوله : (فإن حبس فضاع فلا أجر ولا ضمان وهذا عند الإمام لأنه غير متعد في الحبس فبقي أمانة كما كان عنده، ولا أجر له الهلاك المعقود عليه قبل التسليم وعندهما العين كانت مضمونة قبل الحبس فكذا بعده لكنه بالخيار إن شاء ضمنه غير معمول ولا أجر له، وإن شاء معمولاً وله الأجر قوله : ( ومن لا أثر لعمله كالحمال والملاح لا يحبس للأجر) لأن المعقود عليه نفس العمل وهو غير قائم في العين فلا يتصور حبسه فليس له ولاية الحبس فأفاد أنه لو حبسها ضمنها ضمان الغاصب وصاحبها بالخيار إن شاء ضمنه قيمتها محمولة وله الأجر، وإن شاء غير محمولة فلا أجر له ؛ كذا في الجوهرة.
His saying: (And whoever's work leaves a trace in the object, like the dyer and fuller, he may detain them for the wage) because the contracted object is an attribute subsisting in the cloth, so he has the right of retention to collect the substitute, like in a sale. He (the author) gave it absolutely, so it includes the case where his work only removes dirt by washing, according to the soundest view, because the whiteness was hidden and became apparent by his action, as if he created it in it; thus mentioned Qadi Khan in his commentary. And the author in his Mustasfa corrected, attributing to al-Dhakhira, that he has no right of retention, so the correction differs, and it is appropriate to prefer prohibition, and the author of al-Hidaya affirmed it by saying: washing the cloth is analogous to carrying. And his intent is when the wage is immediate; as for if it is deferred, he has no right of retention for it because delivery is not obligatory upon him at present, so he cannot detain, just as if he sold something for a deferred price, he has no right of retention. And he indicated by his saying 'he detains them' that his work is in his house or shop, so it benefits that if he sewed or dyed it in the hirer's house, he has no right of retention because the garment was delivered to the owner due to the place being in his hand; thus in al-Khulasa, and he is liable for what his hand damaged according to the Imam, even if in the hirer's house, unlike the boatman if the ship sank by his rowing and the owner's goods were in it, where he does not guarantee the goods because it is actually in the owner's hand, and the rowing is an action on the ship not on the goods; so when he was permitted by the owner, he is not transgressing in the cause, so he is not held liable for guarantee; thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. His saying: (And if he detains and it is lost, then no wage and no guarantee) and this according to the Imam because he is not transgressing in the detention, so it remains a trust as it was with him, and no wage for him because the contracted object perished before delivery. And according to the two companions, the object was guaranteed before detention, so likewise after detention, but he has the option: if he wishes, he guarantees it without work and has no wage, and if he wishes, with work and he has the wage. His saying: (And whoever's work has no trace, like the porter and boatman, may not detain for the wage) because the contracted object is the work itself, which does not subsist in the object, so detention is inconceivable, thus he has no authority to detain. So it benefits that if he detains, he guarantees it as a usurper, and its owner has the option: if he wishes, he guarantees its value carried and has the wage, and if he wishes, not carried, so no wage for him; thus in al-Jawhara.
Source pages p. 515

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the right of a worker (ajir) to detain the object of his work for his wage. The author of al-Hidayah distinguishes between two types of workers: those whose work leaves a trace (athar) in the object, like a dyer (sabbagh) or fuller (qassar), and those whose work leaves no trace, like a porter (hammal) or boatman (mallah). For the first type, the worker has the right to detain the object until his wage is paid, because the contracted benefit is an attribute that subsists in the object (such as color or cleanliness), similar to the right of retention in a sale. For the second type, the contracted object is the work itself (nafs al-'amal), which does not remain in the object, so detention is not possible. The passage further discusses details: if the worker's work only removes dirt, the soundest view is that he still has the right of retention because he has brought out what was hidden. However, some scholars like the author of al-Dhakhira hold that he has no such right. The preferred view (mu'tamad) is that he does not have the right to detain (tarjih al-man'). Also, if the wage is deferred (mu'ajjal), the worker cannot detain because delivery is not due immediately. Additionally, if the work was done in the hirer's house, the worker has no right of retention because the object was already delivered. The passage also covers liability: if the worker detains and the object is lost, according to Abu Hanifa he is not liable and gets no wage; according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the worker is a guarantor (damana) but has an option: either guarantee without wage or with wage. For workers without trace, if they detain, they become guarantors like a usurper, and the owner has a similar option.

Key Terms
أثر (athar): A change or effect in the object that subsists after the work is done, like dye or stitching.
حبس (habs): The right to retain possession of an object until payment of a debt or wage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the passage, does a dyer (sabbagh) have the right to detain the cloth for his wage?
A) Yes, always
B) Yes, but only if the wage is immediate
C) No, he does not have the right of detention
D) Yes, but only if the work is done in his own shop

Key Takeaway
The right of detention for workers depends on the presence of a trace in the object; the preferred Hanafi view is that workers with trace should not detain, while those without trace definitely cannot.
